Unit_2_Fundamentals_in_Nursing.pdf</p></div></div></div><div class="stElementContainer element-container st-emotion-cache-kj6hex eu6p4el1" data-testid="stElementContainer" data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT TWO: FUNDAMENTALS IN NURSING PRACTICE</p>
<p>This second unit of the first module lays down principles, concepts and basic procedures to be applied in clinical practice. Most of the content is based on what you have already learnt during your Kenya Enrolled Community Health Nursing course.</p>
<p><strong>This unit is composed of four sections:</strong></p>
<p>Section One: Concept of Infection Prevention and Control.</p>
<p>Section Two: Basic Nursing Procedures.</p>
<p>Section Three: Diagnosis and Treatment of Minor Illnesses.</p>
<p>Section Four: The Principles of Safe Drug Use.</p>
<p><strong>Unit Objectives</strong></p>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the concept of infection prevention and control</li>
<li>Describe basic nursing procedures</li>
<li>Diagnose and treat minor illnesses</li>
<li>Describe the principles of safe drug use</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>SECTION 1: INFECTION PREVENTION AND CONTROL</strong></p>
<p>In this first section you will cover the concept of Infection Prevention and Control.</p>
<p>The focus of infection prevention is to minimise the risk of transmitting infections to patients, service providers, supportive staff, house keeping personnel and members of the community.</p>
<p>The goal of infection prevention is to minimise post procedure infections in patients and prevent transmission of life threatening infections to patients, service providers, auxiliary staff and members of the community (AVSC 1999).</p>
<p><strong>Objectives</strong></p>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>State an overview of infectious diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the disease transmission cycle and those at risk of infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>List some standard precautions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>List common antiseptics, disinfectants and aseptic techniques</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the use and disposal of needles and other sharps</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the processing of instruments and other items</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe decontamination and sterilisation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe the storage of sterile equipment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describe housekeeping and waste disposal</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>The Concept of Infectious Diseases</strong></p>
<p>Over the past few decades Kenya has experienced a drastic change in the pattern of infectious diseases. Some of those that had been eradicated are re-emerging, and new ones are being identified. There have also been sporadic outbreaks of diseases such as cholera, measles, the plague, and yellow fever. New viruses such as the Hepatitis B and C have become increasingly common. The situation has been made worse by the fact that some micro-organisms are rapidly developing resistance to common antibiotics. Hospital acquired infections are on the increase. This drug resistance, combined with the high HIV/AIDS prevalence, makes infection prevention and control extremely important</p>
<p>The World Health Organisation WHO (1996) observes that millions of people all over the world suffer and even die of hospital acquired infections which have become known as nosocomial infections.</p>
<p>These hospital acquired diseases range from trivial to life threatening conditions such as septicaemia. It is thought that this spread may be due to the advance in medicine that exposes patients to more surgical and medical invasive procedures which increase the risk of infection. It is important to note that shortage of resources may have contributed to some nosocomial infections.</p>
<p>Globally the most frequent infections are: surgical wounds infection, lower respiratory tract and urinary tract infections. The emergence of highly infectious diseases such as the Viral Haemorrhagic Fevers (VHF) also increases the risk of hospital acquired infection.</p>
<p>Health care facilities are ideal settings for the transmission of infections because the invasive procedures routinely performed on patients have the potential of introducing micro-organisms into the body.</p>
<p><strong>Who is at Risk of Infection?</strong></p>
<p>The service providers in health care facilities are at high risk because they constantly perform procedures that expose them to infections. They can easily spread an infection they have contracted at the health facility to their families because of poor infection prevention practices.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>The community is also at risk of infections if they come into contact with medical waste such as contaminated sharps, dressings, tissue and chemical waste that have been inappropriately disposed</p>
<p>Everyone who works at a health care facility is potentially at risk of infections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-disease-transmission-cycle">The Disease Transmission Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-disease-transmission-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Infectious agents survive, grow or multiply in a reservoir and then leave the reservoir through a place of exit by a modeof transmission.</p>
<p>The infectious agents then enter the susceptible host through a place of entry.</p>
<p>Micro-organisms are normally present on people's skin, respiratory, intestinal and genital tracts. These micro-organisms are called normal flora. Micro-organisms not normally found on or in the human body are associated with disease and are known as pathogens.</p>
<p>All micro-organisms can cause infection or disease.</p>
<p>This happens when:</p>
<ul>
<li>The normal flora are introduced into an area of the body in which they are not normally found</li>
<li>Pathogens are introduced into the body</li>
<li>Micro-organisms are introduced into the body of a person who is immuno-compromised and thus susceptible to infections</li>
</ul>
<p>The mode of transmission is the easiest point at which to break the disease transmission cycle. In a health care facility, this can be accomplished by following appropriate infection prevention practices, such as washing the hands before and after procedures, practising aseptic technique and correctly processing instruments</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="transmission-of-infection-in-the-health-care-setting">Transmission of Infection in the Health Care Setting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transmission-of-infection-in-the-health-care-setting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the health care setting infection can be transmitted:</p>
<ul>
<li>When the health care worker's skin is pierced or cut by contaminated needles or other sharp instruments</li>
<li>When the health care worker's broken skin (cuts, scratches, rashes, chapped skin, fungal infections) comes into contact with the patient's blood or other body fluids</li>
<li>When the patient's blood or other body fluids are splashed on the healthcare worker's mucous membranes (eyes, nose, mouth)</li>
</ul>
<p>All cases of transmission of Hepatitis B and HIV from patients to health care workers have</p>
<p>occurred through accidents such as needle stick injuries.</p>
<p>Furthermore, as a health worker you can spread infections from one patient to another and from patients to yourself, your family and the community.</p>
<p>Infectious diseases could be minimised or eliminated by adhering to medical principles and practices that reduce cross infection in healthcare settings. The spread of most infections can be controlled by observing basic infection prevention control guidelines and proper and adequate treatment of primary cases.</p>
<p>The WHO's guidelines demand that you should treat all patients as potentially infectious. Furthermore, WHO stipulates proper precaution and use of correct and appropriate protective gear when dealing with or handling blood and blood products, body fluids or contaminated equipment.</p>
<p>According to WHO guidelines, you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Observe and maintain good personal hygiene and wear appropriate attire.</li>
<li>Be vaccinated against vaccine preventable conditions, especially if you are working in high risk areas.</li>
<li>If you work in vulnerable areas, for example areas where you handle cooked food, you should be periodically screened for certain diseases, such as typhoid.</li>
<li>If you are suffering from infectious conditions and you are working with susceptible patients, for example, in an operating room, special care baby unit, or the ICU burns unit, you should be re-deployed until you are cleared of the infection.</li>
</ul>
<p>Having looked at the overview of infection prevention and control, you will now look at it in some more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-can-you-spread-infections-from-one-patient-to-another-or-to-your-family-and-community">How can you spread infections from one patient to another or to your family and community?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-can-you-spread-infections-from-one-patient-to-another-or-to-your-family-and-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If you do not wash your hands before and after contact with patients, or when you do not wash your hands before leaving the health facility and then touch members of your family or household items</li>
<li>When you use surgical instruments, such as needles, syringes and other equipment that have not been processed properly</li>
<li>When medical waste is not disposed of properly, members of the community may come into contact with that waste</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>When you contaminate your clothing or hair in the course of rendering care to patients</li>
<li>When you contract infections and spread them to some members of your family, they will in turn spread them to other members of the family, who in turn will spread them to others in the community</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The focus of infection prevention is to the utilisation of procedures and techniques in the surveillance investigation and compilation of statistical data in order to minimise the spread of infection.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-984a90df.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goal">Goal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The goal of infection prevention is to minimise post procedure infections in patients and prevent transmission of life threatening infections to patients, service providers, auxiliary staff and members of the community (AVSC 1999).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infection-prevention-practices">Infection Prevention Practices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infection-prevention-practices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Adherence to appropriate infection prevention practices breaks the cycle of spreading infections at the mode of transmission stage. This will:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prevent post procedure infections</li>
<li>Result in high quality, safe services</li>
<li>Prevent infections in service providers and supportive staff</li>
<li>Protect the community from infections that originate in health care facilities</li>
<li>Prevent the spread of micro-organisms that are resistant to antibiotics</li>
<li>Lower the cost of health care services</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="standard-precautions">Standard Precautions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#standard-precautions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Standard precautions are a set of clinical practice recommendations designed to help minimise the risk of exposure to infectious materials, such as blood and other body fluids by both patients and staff. They help break the disease transmission cycle at the mode of transmission step.</p>
<p>A standard procedure is a procedure that should be followed routinely at all times. It should apply to every patient regardless of their presumed infection status. This is because you will not be able to tell who is infected with viruses such as HIV or hepatitis. Even the infected persons themselves may not know that they are infected. You should therefore follow the standard precautions when dealing with every patient.</p>
<p>You will now cover these precautions in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hand-washing">Hand Washing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hand-washing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Washing your hands before and after contact with each patient is the single most effective method of preventing/decreasing transfer of micro-organisms between you and the patients within a health facility. This method is easy to follow and is an inexpensive procedure. The purpose of hand washing is to remove soil, organic material and transient micro-organisms from the skin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="think-of-five-appropriate-times-for-washing-your-hands-whilst-at-work">Think of five appropriate times for washing your hands whilst at work.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#think-of-five-appropriate-times-for-washing-your-hands-whilst-at-work" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Immediately after arriving at work</li>
<li>Before examining each patient</li>
<li>After examining each patient</li>
<li>After touching accidentally any instrument or object that might be contaminated with blood or other body fluids</li>
<li>After touching mucous membranes, e.g. eyes, nose, mouth</li>
<li>After un-gloving since hands can be contaminated if gloves contain invisible holes or tears</li>
<li>After using the toilet or latrine</li>
<li>Before eating</li>
<li>Before leaving work at the end of the day</li>
</ul>
<p>The three elements that are essential for effective hand washing are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Soap</li>
<li>Running water</li>
<li>Friction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="four-types-of-hand-washing">Four types of hand washing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#four-types-of-hand-washing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Routine hand washing using plain soap and running water</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Routine hand washing removes transient micro-organisms and soil, blood or other organic material from the hands. This method is appropriate in most situations and the hands should be washed as frequently as possible</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hand-washing-with-antiseptic-and-running-water">Hand washing with antiseptic and running water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hand-washing-with-antiseptic-and-running-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this method, transient micro-organisms and soil are removed.</p>
<p>It kills or inhibits the growth of resident micro-organisms. Moreover, it may reduce the risk of infections in high risk situations, such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>When there is heavy microbial contamination</li>
<li>Before performing invasive procedures such as vein punctures and other aseptic procedures</li>
<li>Before contact with patients who have immune defects, for example, patients with burns, leukaemia etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="alcohol-hand-rub">Alcohol hand rub<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcohol-hand-rub" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Alcohol hand rub kills or inhibits the growth of most transient and resident micro-organisms but does not remove all micro-organisms or soil. It can be used when hand washing with soap and running water is not possible as long as hands are not visibly soiled with dirt, blood or other organic material.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-hand-scrub">Surgical hand scrub<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-hand-scrub" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Scrubbing with antiseptic before beginning surgical procedures will help prevent the growth of micro-organisms for a period of time.</p>
<p>It will also reduce the risk of infections to the patient if the gloves are damaged.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="policy-statement">Policy Statement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#policy-statement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Patients and family members shall be instructed in proper hand washing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient's hands shall be washed before eating, after toileting and when soiled.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The health care facility approved soap shall be used for routine hand washing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Repeat hand washing shall not be done in the same container of water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hands shall be washed under running water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hands shall not be dried on personal clothes, wet and soiled towels. Air blow driers are not recommended.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hands shall be washed immediately on arrival at work.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Whenever there is a chance of contamination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Before putting on gloves for performing clinical procedures such as insertion of IUD or invasive procedures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Before putting on gloves for performing invasive procedures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Between certain procedures on the same patient where soiling of hands is likely, to avoid cross-contamination of body sites.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After contact with items known or considered likely to be contaminated with blood, body fluids, secretions or excretions (e.g. bedpans, urinals, wound dressing), whether or not gloves are worn.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After touching blood, body fluids, secretions excretions, exudates from wounds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Before and after gloves are removed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Before medication preparation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Before preparing, handling, serving or eating food and before feeding a patient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After diapering or toileting children.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When hands are visibly soiled.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After personal body functions such as using the toilet, wiping or blowing one's nose.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Before leaving work.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>You should wash your hands with antimicrobial soap or an antiseptic solution which should then be followed by good rinsing under running water. This is a more effective method of removing and killing transient micro-organisms.</p>
<p>Vigorously rub soaped hands for 15-30 seconds and then rinse under running water.</p>
<p>Plain water removes 50% of transient micro-organisms, while soap removes 80-90% of micro-organisms.</p>
<p>After washing your hands you should dry them with a clean towel or air dry them.</p>
<p>Be aware that shared towels can become contaminated quickly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-protective-equipment">Personal Protective Equipment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-protective-equipment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are physical barriers used to prevent transmission of infection to the patient or from the patient to the persons attending them, for example, gloves, gowns, surgical masks and protective eye wear</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 31 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gloves">Gloves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gloves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Gloves provide a barrier against potentially infectious micro-organisms in blood, other body fluids, and medical waste, thus lowering the risk of transmitting infections to both health care workers and patients. Gloves also protect against hazardous chemical waste. You should wear gloves whenever you may come into contact with patient's blood and other body fluids, for example, while:</p>
<ul>
<li>Providing clinical services</li>
<li>Handling or cleaning used instruments and other items</li>
<li>Performing housekeeping activities</li>
<li>Use a new pair of gloves for each patient! Disposable gloves are used once and then thrown away</li>
<li>Disposable gloves are preferable to renewable gloves because it is difficult to properly process gloves. Disposable gloves should never be processed or reused</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-gloves">TYPES OF GLOVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-gloves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sterile-surgical-gloves-or-high-level-disinfected-surgical-gloves">Sterile Surgical Gloves or High Level Disinfected Surgical Gloves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sterile-surgical-gloves-or-high-level-disinfected-surgical-gloves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These should be worn during all procedures in which your main aim is to avoid introduction of pathogens into the patient, for example during:</p>
<ul>
<li>Surgical procedures</li>
<li>Insertion of Norplant implants</li>
<li>Pelvic examination of women in labour</li>
</ul>
<p>Disposable surgical gloves are recommended for use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="single-use-examination-gloves">Single use examination gloves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#single-use-examination-gloves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Single use means discard gloves after use. These should be worn for all procedures in which you will be in contact with intact mucous membranes, such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>IUCD insertion</li>
<li>Manual vacuum aspiration</li>
<li>Pelvic examination</li>
</ul>
<p>Also where the primary purpose of wearing gloves is to reduce the risk of you being exposed to blood or other body fluids for example:</p>
<ul>
<li>When drawing blood</li>
<li>When working in the laboratory</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="gowns-and-aprons">Gowns and Aprons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gowns-and-aprons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These should be made of waterproof material and worn full size to give maximum protection. They should be used when splashing of blood or other body fluids or when any other potentially infectious materials are anticipated, for example during:</p>
<ul>
<li>Surgical operations</li>
<li>While conducting deliveries</li>
<li>During intubations and sanctioning procedures</li>
<li>Any other procedure/activities where splashing is anticipated</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="masks-and-eye-shields">Masks and Eye Shields<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#masks-and-eye-shields" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These provide some protection against airborne pathogens and shield against splashes. They should be worn during dental surgery, when conducting deliveries and endoscopies or in any other situations where splashing or spattering is anticipated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="headgear-and-boots">Headgear and Boots<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#headgear-and-boots" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Caps are worn full length to cover the head. Boots and shoe covers should be waterproof and should be cleaned frequently. These should be used in operative procedures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="appropriate-and-adequate-instruments-processing">Appropriate and Adequate Instruments Processing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#appropriate-and-adequate-instruments-processing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>While tackling this topic we will deal with the following aspects:</p>
<ul>
<li>Antiseptics and disinfectants</li>
<li>Aseptic technique</li>
<li>Use and disposal of needles and other sharp objects</li>
<li>Decontamination and preparation of chlorine solutions</li>
<li>Cleaning instruments and other items</li>
<li>Sterilisation and storage</li>
<li>High level disinfection and storage</li>
<li>Waste disposal</li>
</ul>
<p>Move on to look at these one by one.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="antiseptics-and-disinfectants">Antiseptics and Disinfectants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antiseptics-and-disinfectants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>An antiseptic is a chemical agent used on the skin and mucous membrane to remove or kill micro-organisms without causing damage or irritation to the skin and mucous membranes. An antiseptic may also prevent the growth and development of micro-organisms.</p>
<p>Antiseptics are not meant to be used on inanimate objects, such as instruments and surfaces (AVSC, 1999). You can use antiseptics for surgical hand scrub, skin preparation as well as cervical and vaginal preparation before a clinical procedure.</p>
<p>Disinfectants are chemical agents used to kill micro-organisms on inanimate objects, such as instruments and surfaces. Disinfectants are not</p>
<p>meant to be used on the skin or mucous membranes (AVSC, 1999).</p>
<p>There are two types of disinfectants: high level and low level.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="high-level-disinfectants">High Level Disinfectants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#high-level-disinfectants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>High level disinfectants kill bacteria, viruses, fungi and some bacterial endospores. Some high level disinfectants can be used to sterilise equipment and if given sufficient time to act, they are able to destroy bacterial endospores that cause diseases such as tetanus and gas gangrene. Bacterial endospores are difficult to kill because of their protective casing or coating.</p>
<p>High level disinfectants are also used for processing instruments and other items.</p>
<p>Do not soak or store cheatly forceps, scissors, scalpel blades and suture needles in a disinfectant solution for a very long time.</p>
<p>Should you need to sterilise them using high level disinfectant solution, soak them only for a specified time, remove, rinse and store dry.</p>
<p>What you should also note is that micro-organisms can live and multiply in disinfectant solutions which can in turn contaminate the instruments and other items, leading to infections. This topic will be covered in more detail later.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="low-level-disinfectants">Low Level Disinfectants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#low-level-disinfectants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Low level disinfectants kill most bacteria and some viruses and fungi but do not kill tuberculosis causing micro-organisms and bacterial endospores. They are used for cleaning surfaces such as floors and countertops. They should not be used for processing instruments and other items.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-antiseptics-and-disinfectants">Common Antiseptics and Disinfectants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-antiseptics-and-disinfectants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are by now aware that the use of antiseptics and disinfectants may vary from hospital to hospital.</p>
<p>Alcohol (60-90% ethyl or isopropyl)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Antimicrobial Spectrum</th><th>Advantages</th><th>Disadvantages</th><th>Comments</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Effective against a broad range of micro-organisms.</td><td>Kills micro-organisms most rapidly.</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Most effective in reducing micro-organisms.</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Effectiveness is only moderately reduced by blood or other organic material.</td><td>Has a drying effect on skin.</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Cannot be used on mucous membranes.</td><td>Cannot be used when skin is dirty.</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Wash the area before applying.</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Must dry skin completely to be effective.</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>The 60-70% strength is most effective because alcohol must be diluted for optimal killing of micro-organisms, it is less drying to skin, and it is less expensive.</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>

Iodophors are a better choice for use in these areas. If iodophor is not available, a product containing chlorhexidine is the best alternative.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Hexachlorophene (Phisohex)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Antimicrobial Spectrum</th><th>Advantages</th><th>Disadvantages</th><th>Comments</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Poor effectiveness against most micro-organisms.</td><td>Has a good, persistent effect with repeated use which remains effective for at least six hours after being applied.</td><td>Potentially toxic to the nervous system. <p>Iodine, including tincture of iodine (iodine and alcohol)</p>

<p>Common High Level Disinfectants</p>
<p>You must have used some high level disinfectants. You will now study the two chemicals most commonly available that are suitable for high level disinfection (HLD) of instruments and other items. These are chlorine and glutaraldehyde.</p>
<p>Chlorine</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-low-level-disinfectants">Common Low Level Disinfectants<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-low-level-disinfectants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Examples of low level disinfectants (LLDs) are phenols (carbolic acid such as phenol, lysol) and quaternary ammonium compounds (berzal conium chloride â€“ zephiron). They are commonly used to disinfect walls, floors and furnishings.</p>
<p>Instruments and items such as cheat forceps, scissors, scalpel blades and suture needles should not be left soaking indefinitely or stored in a disinfectant solution.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aseptic-technique">Aseptic Technique<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aseptic-technique" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During your nursing practice you have probably been performing several sterile procedures such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Wound dressing</li>
<li>Administration of an injection</li>
<li>Removing stitches, staples and clips</li>
<li>Shortening or removing drains</li>
<li>Urinary catheterisation</li>
<li>Surgical asepsis in an operating room</li>
</ul>
<p>Aseptic can be defined as "free from sepsis or germ free".</p>
<p>A technique is a method or skill used for a particular task or technical proficiency. Other definitions of technique are: art, artistry, craft, proficiency, skill, touch.</p>
<p>Weller, (1996) defines aseptic technique as:</p>
<p>"A method of carrying out sterile procedures so that there is the minimum of risk of introducing infection."</p>
<p>This is achieved by the sterility of equipment and a non touch technique. Brunner and Sudarth (1988) state some basic rules with regards to surgical asepsis as follows:</p>
<p>"Only sterile surfaces or articles may touch other sterile surfaces or articles and remain sterile. In contrast, un-sterile contact at any point renders a sterile area contaminated. If there is any doubt about the sterility of an article or area, it is considered un-sterile."</p>
<p>Also note whatever is sterile for one patient can only be used for that patient. Unused sterile supplies must be discarded or re-sterilised if they are to be used again.</p>
<p>You must pour sterile fluids from a point high enough to prevent accidental touching of the receptacle, but this should not be so high as to produce splashing which causes the fluid to touch an unsterile surface then flow back into the receptacle causing contamination.</p>
<p>The aseptic technique is applied when performing sterile procedures whether in general nursing, midwifery or community health nursing.</p>
<p>The practices performed just before or during a clinical procedure include hand washing, surgical hand scrub, using barriers such as gloves and surgical attire, proper preparation of a patient for clinical procedures, maintaining a sterile field, using good surgical technique and maintaining a safer environment in the surgical/procedure area.</p>
<p>You will now look at some of the components that have not been covered, beginning with proper preparation of a patient for a clinical procedure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparing-a-patient-for-clinical-procedures">Preparing a Patient for Clinical Procedures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-a-patient-for-clinical-procedures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You have already been preparing patients for a variety of clinical procedures. You must have used some of the antiseptic solutions that were covered earlier.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-you-use-antiseptic-solution-on-the-patient-s-skin-vagina-or-cervix">why you use antiseptic solution on the patient's skin, vagina or cervix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-you-use-antiseptic-solution-on-the-patient-s-skin-vagina-or-cervix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Destroy or prevent the growth of micro-organisms." You will realise that it is very important to pay proper attention to the preparation of a patient before a procedure because most surgical site infections result from contamination during surgery. To reduce</p>
<p>the risk of infections if you must shave the surgical/procedure site, use antimicrobial soap and water or shave dry. On the other hand, you could shave immediately before the operation, in the operation room or procedure room</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparing-the-skin">Preparing the Skin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-the-skin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Clean the site with soap and water. Wipe the skin in a circular motion, beginning in the centre of the site then moving outwards. Use sterile cotton balls or cotton wool sponges held on sponge forceps. You could use any of the following antiseptics as listed in the preferred order:</p>
<ul>
<li>An iodophor (Betadine); then wait for two minutes and wipe off the excess with sterile dry cotton or gauze</li>
<li>4% Chlorhexidine (Hlbiolens) wipe off excess with sterile, dry cotton or gauze</li>
<li>1-3 % iodine, followed by 60-90% alcohol (ethyl or isopropyl) then allow to air dry</li>
<li>Chlorhexidine with cetrimide (Savlon) wipe off the excess with sterile, dry cotton or gauze</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparing-the-vagina-and-cervix">Preparing the vagina and cervix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-the-vagina-and-cervix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Apply an appropriate antiseptic (iodophor) to the vagina and cervix before passing instruments into the uterus such as IUD insertion, uterine evacuation. Alcohol based antiseptics should not be used on the vagina, cervix or other mucous membranes because they are damaging to these tissues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maintaining-a-sterile-field">Maintaining a Sterile Field<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintaining-a-sterile-field" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Think about how you can maintain a sterile field.</p>
<p>You can maintain a sterile field by placing sterile towels and/or surgical drapes around the surgical/procedures site. Other measures include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Placing only sterile items within the sterile field</li>
<li>Opening, dispensing or transferring sterile items without contaminating them</li>
<li>Considering items located below the level of the draped client to be unsterile</li>
<li>Not allowing sterile personnel to reach across unsterile areas and touch unsterile items</li>
<li>Not allowing unsterile personnel to reach across the sterile field or to touch sterile items</li>
</ul>
<p>Think about how you can maintain a safe environment in the surgical/procedure area.</p>
<p>You are aware that specific rooms have been designed for performing surgical/clinical</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>procedures and processing instruments and other items.</p>
<p>You often hear of dressing room or treatment room, autoclaving room and so on. In these rooms traffic is controlled. Other activities are minimised or prohibited. This is because the number of people and amount of activity in them influences the number of micro-organisms and the risk of infections. You must therefore:</p>
<ul>
<li>Limit the entry of unauthorised individuals to surgical/procedure areas</li>
<li>Close doors and curtains during all procedures</li>
<li>Require that personnel in the surgical area wear clean clothes, a mask, a cap and sturdy footwear</li>
<li>Enclose surgical procedure area to minimise dust and eliminate insects</li>
<li>Air-condition the room if feasible</li>
<li>Disinfect and clean examination/operating tables, instrument trolleys, light handles and any other surfaces that may have been contaminated with blood or other body fluids during a procedure before bringing in a new patient into the room</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="use-and-disposal-of-sharps">Use and Disposal of Sharps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#use-and-disposal-of-sharps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are aware that careless disposal of contaminated sharps can cause infections in the health care facility and the community. Make hypodermic needles and other sharps unusable by incinerating them.</p>
<p>Alternatively the risk of infections can be reduced by decontaminating sharps before disposal, and burying them in a pit to make it difficult for others to scavenge them.</p>
<p>Decontamination is performed by soaking instruments and other items immediately after use, in 0.5% Chlorine solution for ten minutes. Decontamination is done in order to kill viruses (such as Hepatitis B, other hepatitis viruses and HIV) and many other micro-organisms, making instruments and other items easier to clean by preventing blood, other body fluids and tissue from drying on them</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disposing-of-sharps">Disposing of Sharps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disposing-of-sharps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sharps such as needles, scalpels and so on, are to be handled with extreme caution to avoid injuries during use, disposal or reprocessing. Used needles should not be recapped by hand. If necessary use the single hand "scoop" method. With one hand, hold the syringe and use the needle to "scoop up" the cap. Used needles should not be bent or broken after use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="do-not-remove-the-needle-from-the-syringe-by-hand-dispose-of-the-needle-and-attached-syringe-in-a-puncture-resistant-sharps-disposal-container">Do not remove the needle from the syringe by hand. Dispose of the needle and attached syringe in a puncture-resistant sharps disposal container<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-not-remove-the-needle-from-the-syringe-by-hand-dispose-of-the-needle-and-attached-syringe-in-a-puncture-resistant-sharps-disposal-container" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A sharps disposal container may be a heavy cardboard box or an empty plastic or metal container. At all times obey the following rules:</p>
<p>Section 1:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infection-prevention-and-control">Infection Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infection-prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dispose of "sharps disposal containers" when they are three quarters full to reduce the chance of injury when disposing of sharps</li>
<li>Dispose of used sharps immediately after use in designated puncture resistant containers labelled with a biohazard symbol and placed in the area where the items were used, for transport to the incinerator/pit for disposal</li>
<li>These containers should not be located in areas open to the public</li>
<li>Discard used syringes and needles as a unit in the designated puncture resistant container</li>
<li>Hold reusable syringes, needles or sharps in a puncture resistant leak proof container labelled with a biohazard sign for transport to the re-processing area</li>
<li>Do not pick up a handful of sharp instruments simultaneously</li>
<li>Exercise caution when rotating instruments in use</li>
<li>Position sharp end of instruments away from yourself and others</li>
<li>Do not break, recap or manipulate by hand used needles</li>
<li>Wear heavy duty/strong utility gloves during decontamination, cleaning and disinfecting instruments</li>
<li>Contact the supervisor immediately if you are injured by sharps</li>
</ul>
<p>A sharps disposal container may be a heavy cardboard box or an empty plastic or metal container. At all times obey the following rules:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dispose of "sharps disposal containers" when they are three quarters full to reduce the chance of injury when disposing of sharps</li>
<li>Dispose of used sharps immediately after use in designated puncture resistant containers labelled with a biohazard symbol and placed in the area where the items were used, for transport to the incinerator/pit for disposal</li>
<li>These containers should not be located in areas open to the public</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Discard used syringes and needles as a unit in the designated puncture resistant container</li>
<li>Hold reusable syringes, needles or sharps in a puncture resistant leak proof container labelled with a biohazard sign for transport to the re-processing area</li>
<li>Do not pick up a handful of sharp instruments simultaneously</li>
<li>Exercise caution when rotating instruments in use</li>
<li>Position sharp end of instruments away from yourself and others</li>
<li>Do not break, recap or manipulate by hand used needles</li>
<li>Wear heavy duty/strong utility gloves during decontamination, cleaning and disinfecting instruments</li>
<li>Contact the supervisor immediately if you are injured by sharps</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-for-decontaminating-reusable-hypodermic-needles-and-syringes">Steps for Decontaminating Reusable Hypodermic Needles and Syringes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-for-decontaminating-reusable-hypodermic-needles-and-syringes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Take the following steps to decontaminate reusable hypodermic needles and syringes:</p>
<ol>
<li>Drop the needle and syringe into a container of 0.5% chlorine solution, and let them soak for ten minutes.</li>
<li>Remove the needle and syringe from the solution, using cheatle forceps or by hand, if hands are protected by utility gloves.</li>
<li>Rinse by flushing with clean water, or clean immediately.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-injuries-from-needles-and-other-sharps">Management of Injuries from Needles and Other Sharps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-injuries-from-needles-and-other-sharps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Wash needle stick cuts with soap and water.</li>
<li>Flush the nose, mouth or skin with water if splashed with blood or body fluid.</li>
<li>Irrigate the eyes with water or saline if splashed with body fluid.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-exposure-prophylaxis">Post-exposure Prophylaxis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-exposure-prophylaxis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Post-exposure prophylaxis with drugs can reduce the risk of transmission of some blood borne pathogens. Following exposure to blood or other body fluids, a number of factors have to be considered. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The infection status of the source patient (the patient whose blood or other body fluids are involved)</li>
<li>The type of exposure for example: a splash to the skin, or a deep puncture wound by a very bloody needle</li>
<li>Whether or not the exposed person has been vaccinated against Hepatitis B, how much time has passed since the exposure, the availability of the required drugs or other therapy</li>
</ul>
<p>The prophylaxis will include:</p>
<ul>
<li>For Hepatitis B: Hepatitis immune globulin and Hepatitis B vaccine can reduce the risk of infection after exposure to blood and other body fluids containing the Hepatitis B virus</li>
<li>For HIV: Several antiretroviral drugs are used either alone or in combination. These include: Zidovudine (AZT, Retrovir), Lamivudine (3TC, Epivir) and Nelfinavir (viracept)</li>
<li>For Hepatitis C: There is no post exposure prophylaxis available for Hepatitis C</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="giving-injections">Giving Injections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#giving-injections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In order to reduce the risk of transmitting infections between patients, you should always adhere to the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Every time you give an injection, use a new or correctly processed hypodermic needle and syringe.</li>
<li>Do not change the needle without changing the syringe between patients.</li>
<li>Reusing the same syringe to give injections to many clients is not a safe practice</li>
</ul>
<p>While administering intravenous fluids you have the responsibility to avoid the transmission of infections.</p>
<p>You must therefore do the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Unhook the needle or catheter from the IV line and dispose of it in a sharps disposal container</li>
<li>Throw away any remaining fluid</li>
<li>Do not use the same IV line and fluid bag/bottle with multiple clients</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="use-of-multi-dose-vials">Use of Multi Dose Vials<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#use-of-multi-dose-vials" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Before you fill a syringe from a multiple dose vial:</p>
<ul>
<li>Check the vial to be sure there are no leaks or cracks.</li>
<li>Check the solution to be sure it is not cloudy and that there is no particulate matter in the vial.</li>
<li>Wipe the top of the vial with a fresh cotton swab soaked with 60-70% alcohol.</li>
<li>Allow to dry.</li>
</ul>
<p>To reduce the risk of transmitting infections between patients:</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Always use a sterile needle and syringe every time medication is withdrawn from a multiple dose vial. Reusing the same syringe to give injections to multiple patients, even if the needle is changed is not a safe practice.</li>
<li>Do not leave a needle inserted in the vial cap for purpose of withdrawing drugs from a multiple dose vial. This provides a direct route for micro-organisms to enter the vial.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="processing-of-instruments-and-items">Processing of Instruments and Items<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#processing-of-instruments-and-items" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are now going to cover the processing of instruments in more detail. It is important to bear in mind that when you are involved in the processing of instruments and other items, you are at high risk of infection. You therefore need to take appropriate steps to reduce this risk.</p>
<p>You are at risk of exposure to blood or other body fluids when processing instruments and other items.</p>
<p>You are at a risk of exposure if:</p>
<ul>
<li>You have open cuts on the hands or forearms</li>
<li>You have chapped or cracked hands</li>
<li>You get injuries from needle sticks or other sharp instruments such as scalpels</li>
<li>There is splashing of blood or other body fluids contained on the instruments or other items onto mucous membranes such as the eyes</li>
</ul>
<p>The measures you should take to protect yourself when handling instruments and other items focus on:</p>
<ul>
<li>Destroying as many micro-organisms as possible early in the process</li>
<li>Preventing blood and other body fluids from coming in to contact with the skin or membranes</li>
</ul>
<p>Always wear gloves when handling potentially contaminated instruments and other items</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="steps-of-processing-instruments-and-other-items">Steps of Processing Instruments and Other Items<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-of-processing-instruments-and-other-items" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Processing instruments and other items involves steps that reduce the risk of transmitting infections from used instruments and other items, to you, other health workers and patients.</p>
<p>These steps are decontamination, cleaning and either sterilisation or high level disinfection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="decontamination">Decontamination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#decontamination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Decontamination is the first step in processing instruments and other items for re-use. Decontamination kills viruses and many micro-organisms, making the instruments and other items safe to handle by the staff who clean them. Decontamination also makes instruments and other items easier to clean by preventing blood, other body fluids and tissue from drying on them. Decontamination is done by soaking instruments and other items immediately after use, in a 0.5% chlorine solution for 10 minutes immediately after use (AVSC, 1999). A container of this solution should be kept in every operating room and procedure room so that used items can be placed directly into the bucke</p>
<p>Prepare a new chlorine solution at the beginning of each day or when the solution looks as though it needs to be changed, such as when it becomes heavily contaminated with blood or other body fluids or becomes cloudy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparing-a-chlorine-solution">Preparing a Chlorine Solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-a-chlorine-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A chlorine solution can be made from household liquid bleach (sodium hypochlorite), commonly known as JIK, or chlorine compounds available in powder form (calcium hypochlorite, chloramines, or chlorinated lime) or tablet (sodium dichloroisocyanurate) form. This is because of their low cost and wide availability. Chlorine solutions prepared from liquid or powdered bleach are recommended for decontamination.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-is-chlorine-the-most-widely-used-product-for-preventing-infections-in-health-care-settings">Why is chlorine the most widely used product for preventing infections in health care settings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-is-chlorine-the-most-widely-used-product-for-preventing-infections-in-health-care-settings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is a proven and powerful killer of micro-organisms</li>
<li>It deodorises</li>
<li>It is economical to use</li>
<li>It leaves no poisonous residue and is not poisonous to people in the concentrations it is used</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparing-a-chlorine-solution">Preparing a Chlorine Solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-a-chlorine-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>% Chlorine in liquid bleach -1=total parts of water for each bleach
% Chlorine desired</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example">Example<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To make a 0.5% Chlorine Solution from 3.5% bleach:</p>
<p>3.5% -1=7-1= 6 parts of water in each part of bleach</p>
<p>0.5%</p>
<p>Therefore, you must add one part bleach to six parts water to make 0.5% chlorine solutions.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>'Parts' can be used for any unit of measure, for example, an ounce, a litre, or a gallon or any container used for measuring such as a pint.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparing-a-dilute-chlorine-solution-using-bleach-powder">Preparing a Dilute Chlorine Solution Using Bleach Powder<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-a-dilute-chlorine-solution-using-bleach-powder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If using bleach powder, calculate the ratio of bleach to water by using the following formula:</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi><mtext>&nbsp;chlorinedesired</mtext></mrow><mtext>Number&nbsp;of&nbsp;grams&nbsp;of&nbsp;%&nbsp;chlorine&nbsp;in&nbsp;bleach&nbsp;powder&nbsp;powder&nbsp;for&nbsp;each&nbsp;litre&nbsp;of&nbsp;water</mtext></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{\% \text{ chlorinedesired}}{\text{Number of grams of \% chlorine in bleach powder powder for each litre of water}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.3074em; vertical-align: -0.8804em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.427em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">Number&nbsp;of&nbsp;grams&nbsp;of&nbsp;%&nbsp;chlorine&nbsp;in&nbsp;bleach&nbsp;powder&nbsp;powder&nbsp;for&nbsp;each&nbsp;litre&nbsp;of&nbsp;water</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">%</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;chlorinedesired</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">â€‹</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8804em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example">Example<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If you need to make a 0.5% chlorine solution from calcium hypochlorite powder containing 35% active chlorine.</p>
<p>Try to calculate how many grams of powder for each litre of water using the formula above.</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mn>0.5</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>35</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>1000</mn><mo>=</mo><mn>0.0143</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>1000</mn><mo>=</mo><mn>14.3</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{0.5\%}{35\%} \times 1000 = 0.0143 \times 1000 = 14.3</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.1686em;
