vertical-align: -0.7416em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.427em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">35%</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0.5%</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">â€‹</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7416em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1000</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">0.0143</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">1000</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">14.3</span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>Therefore, you must dissolve 14.3 grams of calcium hypochlorite powder in each litre of water used to make 0.5% chlorine solution. When bleach powder is used, the resulting chlorine solution is likely to be cloudy (milky).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning">Cleaning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the second step when processing instruments. It starts by scrubbing with a brush, detergent and water before instruments and other items are sterilised or high level disinfected to remove blood, other body fluids, organic material, tissue, and dirt.</p>
<p>Cleaning greatly reduces the number of micro-organisms including bacteria endospores on instruments and other items.</p>
<p>This is a crucial step in processing instruments and other items. If cleaning has not been done, sterilisation and high level disinfection (HLD) may not be effective because:</p>
<ul>
<li>Micro-organisms trapped in organic material may be protected and survive the sterilisation or HLD process</li>
<li>Organic material and dirt can make the chemicals used in chemical sterilisation and HLD less effective</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-of-cleaning">Steps of cleaning:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-of-cleaning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Wear utility gloves, goggles, a mask and protective eyewear when cleaning instruments and other items.</li>
<li>Using a soft brush, detergent and water and scrub instrument and other items vigorously to completely remove all blood, other body fluids, tissue and other foreign matter.</li>
<li>Hold instruments and other items under the surface of the water while scrubbing and cleaning to avoid splashing.</li>
<li>Disassemble instruments and other items with multiple parts, and be sure to brush in the grooves, teeth and joints of instruments and other items, where organic material can collect and stick.</li>
<li>Rinse instruments and other items thoroughly with clean running water to remove all detergents.</li>
<li>Allow instruments and other items to air dry, or dry with a clean towel. Instruments and other items should be dry before chemical high level disinfection to avoid diluting the chemicals, which may decrease their effectiveness. Instruments and other items to be high level disinfected by boiling or steaming do not need to be dried first</li>
</ul>
<p>Thorough rinsing after cleaning is important, particularly with chemical sterilisation or high level disinfection (HLD), because detergents can reduce the effectiveness of these chemicals.</p>
<p>It is important to dry instruments and other items after cleaning them. The water from instruments and other items dilutes the chemicals used for chemical sterilisation or HLD, making that process ineffective. If instruments and other items will be high level disinfected by boiling or steaming, drying is not necessary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="use-of-detergents">Use of Detergents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#use-of-detergents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Detergents are important for effective cleaning. Water alone does not remove proteins, oils or grease. When the detergent is dissolved in water it breaks and suspends oil and grease, making them easy to remove by cleaning.</p>
<p>Do not use hand soap for cleaning instruments and other items, because fatty acids contained in the soap will react with the minerals of hard water, leaving a residue or scum that is difficult to remove.</p>
<p>Avoid using steel wool or abrasive cleaners such as Vim or cement as they scratch or pit metal or stainless steel, which results in grooves that can collect micro-organisms. This also increases the potential for corrosion of the instruments.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sterilisation">Sterilisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sterilisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the process that eliminates all micro-organisms such as bacteria, viruses, fungi and parasites, including bacterial endospores.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Sterilisation is recommended for instruments and other items that come into contact with the bloodstream or tissues under the skin.</p>
<p>Sterilisation can be performed using steam under pressure (autoclaving or moist heat), dry heat or chemicals.</p>
<p>Boiling and flaming are not effective sterilisation techniques because they do not effectively kill all micro-organisms. The effectiveness of sterilisation depends on:</p>
<ul>
<li>The amount and type of micro-organisms</li>
<li>Absence of organic material (blood, other body fluids and tissues) or other matter such as dirt present on the instrument or other items</li>
<li>The potential the item has to hide or conceal micro-organisms</li>
</ul>
<p>You are therefore to clean instruments and other items thoroughly before sterilisation to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reduce the number of micro-organisms</li>
<li>Eliminate blood, other body fluids, or tissue remains</li>
<li>Remove contaminants that may collect in joints, grooves and teeth of instruments and other items</li>
</ul>
<p>Sterilisation is preferable to high level disinfection for instruments and other items that come into contact with the bloodstream and tissues, because it kills micro-organisms including bacterial endospores</p>
<p>You will now move on to cover the three types of sterilisation one by one, starting with steam sterilisation</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Decontaminate, clean and dry all instruments and other items to be sterilised.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open or unlock all joined instruments and other items, for example, hemostats.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disassemble scissors with sliding or multiple parts to allow steam to reach all surfaces of the item. Do not arrange the instruments and other items tightly together, or wrap gloves into tight balls because steam will not reach all surfaces.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wrap instruments and other items in two layers of paper, cotton or muslin fabric before steam sterilisation. If you are using a drum, make sure the holes are open</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arrange all packs, drums or unwrapped items in the chamber of the autoclave in a way that allows steam to circulate freely.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Always follow the manufacturer's instructions on how to operate the autoclave but sterilise wrapped items for 30 minutes and unwrapped items for 20 minutes at 121Â° C (250Â°F) and 106 Kpa (15 lb/in2) pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the autoclave is automatic, the heat will shut off and the pressure will begin to fall once the sterilisation cycle is complete.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the autoclave is not automatic, turn off the heat or remove the autoclave from the heat source after 30 minutes if items are wrapped, or after 20 minutes if items are unwrapped. Wait until the pressure gauge reads "zero" to open the autoclave.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open the lid or door to allow the remaining steam to escape. Leave instrument packs or items in the autoclave until they dry completely.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Remove the packs, drums or unwrapped items from the autoclave using sterile pick ups.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place packs or drums on a surface padded with paper or fabric until they are cool to prevent condensation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wait until the packs, drums or items reach room temperature before storing.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="storage-of-autoclaved-items-wrapped-items">Storage of Autoclaved Items Wrapped Items<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#storage-of-autoclaved-items-wrapped-items" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Shelf life is the length of time a wrapped sterile item is considered sterile. Shelf life depends on whether or not a contaminating event occurs. Shelf life is affected by a number of factors which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Type of packaging material used</li>
<li>Cleanliness of the store</li>
<li>Humidity in the store</li>
<li>Temperature of the storage area</li>
<li>Storing the packs on open or closed shelves</li>
<li>Usage of dust proof covers</li>
</ul>
<p>Storage time and handling of sterile packs should be kept to a minimum, since the likelihood of handling and contamination increases over time. Place sterile packs in closed cabinets in areas that are not heavily trafficked, have moderate temperature and are dry.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unwrapped-items">Unwrapped Items<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unwrapped-items" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unwrapped items should be used immediately after removal from the autoclave. They can also be kept in a covered, sterile container for up to one week.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dry-heat-sterilisation-or-hot-air-oven-electric-oven">Dry Heat Sterilisation or Hot-Air Oven (Electric Oven)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dry-heat-sterilisation-or-hot-air-oven-electric-oven" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the method of sterilisation that requires heat for a specific period of time.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>This method is used for sterilising glass or metal objects because high temperatures are necessary. The steps to be followed in dry heat sterilisation are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Decontamination: clean and dry all instruments and other items to be sterilised.</li>
<li>Wrap the instruments and other items using foil or double layered cotton or muslin fabric on a tray or shelf.</li>
<li>Put unwrapped instruments and other items on a metal tray or shelf.</li>
<li>Place instruments and other items in the oven and heat to the designated temperature. The oven must have a thermometer or temperature gauge</li>
<li>Ensure that the designated temperature is reached:</li>
</ol>
<table><thead><tr><th>Temperature</th><th>Time</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>170Â°C (340Â°F)</td><td>1 hour</td></tr><tr><td>160Â°C (320Â°F)</td><td>2 hours</td></tr><tr><td>150Â°C (300Â°F)</td><td>2Â½ hours</td></tr><tr><td>140Â°C (285Â°F)</td><td>3 hours</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ol start="6">
<li>Leave instruments and other items in the oven to cool before removing.</li>
<li>When they are cool, remove instruments and other items using sterile pickups.</li>
<li>Immediately use unwrapped items.</li>
<li>Store wrapped items (storage procedure is as discussed under steam sterilisation).</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-sterilisation">Chemical Sterilisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-sterilisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the method of sterilisation used for instruments and other items that are heat sensitive or when heat sterilisation is unavailable. Instruments and other items can be sterilised by soaking them in a chemical solution such as glutaraldehyde, followed by rinsing in sterile water.</p>
<p>Glutaraldehyde is irritating to the skin, eyes and respiratory tract. Wear gloves and limit your exposure time. Keep the area well ventilated when using it. Always follow manufacturer's instructions before use</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="high-level-disinfection-hld">High Level Disinfection (HLD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#high-level-disinfection-hld" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the process that eliminates all microorganisms (including bacteria, viruses, fungi and parasites), but does not reliably kill all bacterial endospores which cause tetanus and gas gangrene.</p>
<p>HLD is suitable for instruments and other items that will come into contact with broken skin or intact mucous membranes.</p>
<p>HLD can be performed by boiling, use of chemicals or steaming</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="high-level-disinfection-by-boiling">High Level Disinfection by Boiling<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#high-level-disinfection-by-boiling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Steps of HLD by Boiling:</p>
<ol>
<li>Decontaminate and clean all instruments and other items to be high level disinfected.</li>
<li>Completely submerge all instruments and other items in the water in the pot or boiler. Open all hinged instruments and other items and dissemble those with sliding or multiple parts. Place any bowls and containers upright, not upside down, and fill with water.</li>
<li>Cover the pot or close the lid of the boiler and bring the water to a gentle, rolling boil.</li>
<li>When water comes to a rolling boil, start timing for 20 minutes. Use a timer or make sure to record the time that the boiling begins. Do NOT add or remove anything until 20 minutes are over.</li>
<li>Lower the heat to keep the water at a gentle rolling boil; too vigorous a boil will cause the instruments to bounce against each other and around the boiler. Lowering the heat at this level of the procedure saves fuel/energy.</li>
<li>After 20 minutes remove instruments using dry, high level disinfected cheatle forceps in a sterile (or high level disinfected) container. Protect from dust and insects. Allow to air dry before use or storage. They can only be used within one week provided they are properly stored.</li>
</ol>
<p>Never leave the instruments in water. They can become contaminated as the water cools down.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="high-level-disinfection-using-chemicals">High Level Disinfection Using Chemicals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#high-level-disinfection-using-chemicals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Instruments and other items must be completely submerged in chemical solution. All hinged instruments must be disassembled.</li>
<li>Soak for 20 minutes, starting from the time when you dropped the instruments into the chemical.</li>
<li>Do not add or remove anything once the timing begins.</li>
<li>Rinse all instruments thoroughly with sterile water before use.</li>
</ul>
<p>It is important to perform these steps in the appropriate order. Study the graphic illustrating this order.</p>
<p>To avoid contaminating instruments and other items after sterilisation or HLD, proper storage is as critical as properly processing the items.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-2e3f7d56.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="housekeeping">Housekeeping<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#housekeeping" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You may be wondering why should you learn house keeping and yet you are working in a health facility. Ask yourself, what is housekeeping?</p>
<p>Housekeeping refers to the general cleaning of baths, sinks, wash basins, beds, tables, floors, walls and other service areas.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-your-role-in-housekeeping">What is Your Role in Housekeeping?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-your-role-in-housekeeping" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are to ensure that a clean environment is achieved. Those charged with the cleaning responsibility remove visible dust and dirt routinely with water and detergent.</p>
<p>When it comes to micro biological control of the health care facility environment it relies on maintenance of smooth, dry and intact surfaces, prompt cleaning of spillage of body fluids, secretions and excretions and prompt removal of these substances from patient treatment areas.</p>
<p>Cleaning and maintenance prevent the build up of soil, dust or other foreign material that can harbour pathogens and support their growth. Cleaning is accomplished with water, detergents and mechanical action. It reduces or eliminates the reservoirs of potential pathogenic micro-organisms.</p>
<p>Warm, soapy water is adequate for cleaning areas not directly involved in patient care such as offices and duty rooms.</p>
<p>A disinfectant is required when cleaning areas with a large number of pathogens such as isolation areas, toilets, surfaces contaminated with infected body fluid spillages or areas where susceptible patients are housed such as operating rooms, the neonatal unit, ICU or burns unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning-routine">Cleaning Routine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning-routine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cleaning routine will depend on whether the area has a low risk or high risk of infection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="low-risk-areas">Low Risk Areas<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#low-risk-areas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are areas such as walls, ceilings and floors. Clean walls and ceilings with water and detergent using a damp cloth.</p>
<p>Ensure routine damp dusting is performed. Always keep surfaces dry. Wipe chairs, lamps, tabletops and counters with a damp cloth, water and detergent.</p>
<p>Clean the floors regularly to keep them clean, using detergent and water, do not use dry brooms to avoid raising dust</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="high-risk-areas">High Risk Areas<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#high-risk-areas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To clean sinks, use a disinfectant cleaning solution with a cloth or brush, then rinse with clean water.</p>
<p>When cleaning toilets and latrines wear utility gloves and rubber boots. Use a disinfectant cleaning solution, scrub daily or as required with a separate cloth or brush.</p>
<p>Wear rubber gloves when cleaning waste containers. Use a detergent solution, scrub to remove soil and organic material. As a supervisor you may be required to demonstrate what you would wish to be done.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cleaning-solutions">Cleaning Solutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cleaning-solutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Solutions used for cleaning in a health facility include</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="plain-detergent-and-water">Plain Detergent and Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plain-detergent-and-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is used for low risk areas and general cleaning tasks. Detergents remove dirt and organic material and dissolve or suspend grease and oil which can then easily be removed by scrubbing</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="0-5-sodium-hypochloride-solution">0.5% Sodium Hypochloride Solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#0-5-sodium-hypochloride-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>(disinfectant solution)</p>
<p>Disinfectants rapidly kill or inactivate micro-organisms during the cleaning process. They are also used to decontaminate an area so that it is safer for staff to clean. Other alternative disinfectants containing 5% carbolic acid such as phenol or lysol can be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disinfectant-detergent-cleaning-solution">Disinfectant/Detergent Cleaning Solution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disinfectant-detergent-cleaning-solution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>This solution contains a disinfectant, a detergent and water. It is used for cleaning areas that may be contaminated with infectious materials.</p>
<p>The solution must contain both a disinfectant and a detergent. Disinfectants rapidly kill or inactivate infectious micro-organisms during the cleaning process. Detergents, on the other hand, remove dirt and organic material, which cannot be done by water or disinfectants alone. Your responsibility will therefore include providing adequate resources such as brooms, dusting cloths, detergents, disinfectants and protective gear for the supportive staff who are charged with the cleaning of the health facility. You will also need to supervise and guide them appropriately so that the health facility remains clean at all items.</p>
<p>Always wear gloves, preferably heavy utility gloves, and sturdy shoes when cleaning.</p>
<p>Waste Disposal</p>
<p>There are three types of waste found in health care facilities</p>
<p>General Waste</p>
<p>This is non-hazardous waste that poses no risk of injury or infections, for example, uncontaminated paper, boxes, packaging materials, bottles, plastic containers and food-related trash</p>
<p>Medical Waste</p>
<p>This is material generated in the diagnosis, treatment, and/or immunisation of clients. This may include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Blood, blood products and other body fluids as well as materials containing fresh or dried blood or body fluids such as bandages and surgical sponges.</li>
<li>Organic waste such as human tissue, body parts, placentas and products of conception.</li>
<li>Sharps (used and unused) such as hypodermic and suture needles, scalpel blades, blood tubes, pipettes, and other glass items that have been in contact with potentially infectious materials such as glass slides and cover slips</li>
</ul>
<p>Hazardous Chemical Waste</p>
<p>This is chemical waste that is potentially toxic or poisonous, for example cleaning products, some disinfectants, cytotoxic drugs, and radioactive compounds.</p>
<p>Disposal of medical and hazardous chemical waste requires special attention in order to maintain a safe and pleasant environment.</p>
<p>This is important in order to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Minimise the spread of infections and reduce the risk of accidental injury to staff, patients, visitors and the local community</li>
<li>Help provide an aesthetically pleasing atmosphere</li>
<li>Reduce odours</li>
<li>Reduce the chances of attracting insects and animals</li>
<li>Reduce the likelihood of contaminating the soil or ground water with chemicals or micro-organi</li>
</ul>
<p>Anyone who handles medical or hazardous chemical waste from the time it is thrown out by a service provider until it reaches the site of disposal is at risk of infections or injury. This includes a large percentage of staff who collect and remove waste, both inside and outside the health care facilities. Those reporting high rates of medical waste related injuries include nurses, midwives, supportive staff, cleaning and maintenance staff. Thus it is advisable that these staff are vaccinated against Hepatitis B. Members of the community also face exposure to potentially infectious medical waste when contaminated dressings, sharps and other waste are not disposed of properly. Often children while playing risk injury and infections. Lack of proper waste disposal practices also put the community at risk of infections when waste such as syringes and needles are scavenged.</p>
<p>Managing Solid Medical Waste</p>
<p>There are four aspects of medical waste management:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sorting</li>
<li>Handling</li>
<li>Interim Storage</li>
<li>Disposal</li>
</ul>
<p>Sorting</p>
<p>Sorting the waste at the point at which it is generated can greatly reduce the amount that needs special handling, thus reducing risks. Ensure that separate containers are used for disposing of general and medical waste. Use coloured plastic containers/bags, painted drums or labels that can be easily read to help distinguish between general and medical containers. For example, use red containers/plastic bags for medical waste.</p>
<p>Handling</p>
<p>Handle medical waste as little as possible before disposal. Empty waste containers in operating rooms,</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>procedure rooms, toilets, latrines and sluice rooms when they become three quarters full (at least once daily). Do not collect medical waste from client care areas by empting it into open carts or wheelbarrows. This may lead to contamination of the surroundings and scavenging of waste. This may also increase the risk of injury to staff, patients and visitors.</p>
<p>Always wear heavy utility gloves and shoes when handling medical waste. Always wash your hands after handling waste and after removing your gloves</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="interim-storage">Interim Storage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interim-storage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If it is necessary to store medical waste on site before disposal:</p>
<ul>
<li>Place waste in an area that is minimally accessible to staff, patients and visitors.</li>
<li>Make sure all containers have lids.</li>
<li>Cover the containers so that insects, rodents and other animals cannot get into them.</li>
<li>Plan for only short term storage (usually for several hours), but no more than one or two days.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disposal">Disposal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disposal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When possible, medical waste should be disposed of on the premises. This allows staff that understand the risks involved to supervise the disposal process. Burning is preferable to burying medical waste. This is because high temperatures destroy micro-organisms and reduce the volume of waste. Burning in an incinerator or oil drum is recommended. Open burning is not recommended, as it causes scattering of waste which is dangerous and unattractive. If open burning must be done, carry the waste to the site just before burning, and burn it in a small, designated area. Remain with the fire until it is extinguished.</p>
<p>If medical waste cannot be burned on the site, burial is the next best option. Burial is feasible only when there is sufficient ground to accommodate the amount of medical waste generated at the facility. The pit should be surrounded by a fence or a wall to limit access to it and to prevent scavenging.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-waste-can-be-taken-to-the-community-waste-disposal-site">General waste can be taken to the community waste disposal site<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-waste-can-be-taken-to-the-community-waste-disposal-site" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="general-guidelines-for-disposal-of-medical-waste">General Guidelines for Disposal of Medical Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-guidelines-for-disposal-of-medical-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Use washable, leak proof containers for disposal of medical waste in rooms and procedure rooms.</p>
<p>Plastic or galvanised metal containers with covers are the best type because they are not likely to corrode. Use small receptacles that use step on levers/pedals to open the cover.</p>
<ul>
<li>Always keep waste containers in convenient places for users.</li>
<li>Empty the container daily or when it is three quarters full. Never put hands into containers with medical waste.</li>
<li>Always dispose of medical waste correctly; never simply throw it outside or leave it in an open pile.</li>
<li>Always wear heavy utility gloves and shoes when handling and transporting medical waste.</li>
<li>Wash both the gloves and your hands afterwards.</li>
<li>Wash containers used for medical waste with a disinfectant cleaning solution and rinse them with water daily (or move often if they are visibly contaminated after the medical waste is dumped).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disposal-of-sharps-liquid-medical-waste-and-hazardous-chemical-waste">Disposal of Sharps, Liquid Medical Waste and Hazardous Chemical Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disposal-of-sharps-liquid-medical-waste-and-hazardous-chemical-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sharps, liquid medical waste, and hazardous chemical waste require special disposal procedures.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sharps">Sharps<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sharps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All used sharps are to be disposed of in puncture resistant containers. Puncture resistant containers can be made out of a heavy cardboard box, an empty plastic jug or a metal container. Sharps containers should be located close to the place in which procedures are performed so that staff do not have to walk across the room carrying used sharps. Keep a sharps disposal container in the laundry in case sharps are found in linen.</p>
<p>Close sharps containers securely when they are three quarters full. If the containers become full, people may push the sharps into the containers, which may cause injury.</p>
<p>Sharps are not destroyed by burning, therefore, you need to render them harmless by placing needles, plastic syringes and scalpels in a metal container. Then, when the container is three quarters full, pour in fuel, ignite and burn it until the fire goes out on its own.</p>
<p>Plastic syringes will melt and, when they cool, become a solid block of plastic, with the sharps embedded in the block. The block can then be buried.</p>
<p>Decontaminate the sharps and bury them in a pit to make it difficult for others to scavenge them. If it is not possible to bury all medical</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>waste on-site, sharps should be given first priority for burial, since they pose the biggest risk of injury and infections.</p>
<p>Always wear heavy utility gloves and shoes when handling or transporting sharps disposal containers. Wash both the gloves before ungloving and your hands afterwards</p>
<p>To reduce the risk of needle stick pricks, never bend, break or remove needles from the syringe before disposal and do not routinely recap needles</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="liquid-medical-waste">Liquid Medical Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#liquid-medical-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When carrying or disposing of liquid medical waste, be careful to avoid splashing the waste on yourself, other people or surfaces. Carefully pour liquid waste down a sink, drain, flushable toilet or latrine. If this is not possible bury it in a pit. Rinse the sink, drain, or toilet thoroughly with water to remove residual waste, again avoiding splashing. Clean with a disinfectant cleaning solution at the end of each day, or more frequently if heavily used or soiled.</p>
<p>Decontaminate the container that held the liquid waste by filling it with a 0.5% chlorine solution and soaking it for 10 minutes before washing. Always wear heavily utility gloves and shoes when handling or transporting liquid medical waste. Wash both the gloves before ungloving and your hands afterwards.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hazardous-chemical-waste">Hazardous Chemical Waste<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hazardous-chemical-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cleaning solutions and disinfectants, such as glutaraldehyde, should be handled as described for liquid medical waste. Rinse containers thoroughly with water, wash glass containers with detergent and water, rinse thoroughly, and reuse. Do not reuse plastic containers. Always wear heavy utility gloves and shoes when handling or transporting hazardous chemical waste. Wash both the gloves and your hands afterwards.</p>
<p>Disposing of cytotoxic chemicals and radioactive waste requires special consideration beyond the scope of this training course.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-basic-nursing-procedures">SECTION 2: BASIC NURSING PROCEDURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-basic-nursing-procedures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In section one, you covered the concepts of infection prevention and control, which you will apply in nursing practice.</p>
<p>In this section, you will cover some of the basic procedures which include lifting and moving patients; collection of specimens; neurological assessment; taking vital signs; drug administration; incision and drainage; monitoring intravenous fluids; care for the terminally ill and last offices</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the lifting and moving of patients</li>
<li>Discuss the collection of specimens</li>
<li>Explain how to make neurological assessment on a patient</li>
<li>Describe drug administration</li>
<li>Manage incisions and drainages</li>
<li>Discuss the monitoring of intravenous fluids</li>
<li>Discuss the care of the terminally ill</li>
<li>Discuss last offices</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="nursing-practice-1-of-2">Nursing Practice (1 of 2)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-practice-1-of-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Nursing practice involves the application of knowledge and skills that improve an individual's level of health. In view of this, all nurses, regardless of their level of educational preparation, learn basic skills that are fundamental to the practice of nursing.</p>
<p>In unit one of this module you studied the definition of nursing. The American Nurses Association (1980) states that, "Nursing is the diagnosis and treatment of human responses to actual or potential health problems. Nursing involves skills that are beneficial to sick or well individuals."</p>
<p>You are being prepared to provide services in many diverse settings such as hospitals, schools, industry and home care.</p>
<p>The major goals of nursing are to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Promote health and prevent diseases</li>
<li>Restore health</li>
<li>Relieve suffering</li>
</ul>
<p>The nursing skills help patients to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Breathe normally</li>
<li>Eat and drink adequately</li>
<li>Eliminate body wastes</li>
<li>Move and maintain desirable postures</li>
<li>Sleep and rest</li>
<li>Select suitable clothing, dress and undress</li>
<li>Maintain body temperature within normal range by adjusting clothing and modifying the environment</li>
<li>Keep the body clean and well groomed and protect the integument</li>
<li>Communicate with others in expressing emotions, needs fears or options</li>
<li>Worship according to ones faith</li>
<li>Work in such a way that there is a sense of accomplishment</li>
<li>Play or participate in various forms of recreation</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Learn, discover and satisfy the curiosity that leads to normal health and use of the available health facilities</li>
</ul>
<p>In the provision of comprehensive care you will be required to apply sciences such as anatomy, physiology, sociology and psychology. You will also be required to incorporate certain skills such as assessment, caring, counselling, and comforting skills.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lifting-and-moving-patients">Lifting and Moving Patients<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lifting-and-moving-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="basic-guidelines-when-transferring-a-patient">Basic Guidelines when Transferring a Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-guidelines-when-transferring-a-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Certain techniques are used when transferring a patient to help prevent injury to the patient as well as to the nurse.</p>
<p>The basic recommended guidelines for you to follow are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Know the patient's diagnosis, capabilities, weaknesses and any movement they are not allowed to undertake.</li>
<li>Put on braces and other devices a patient may use before getting them out of bed.</li>
<li>Plan exactly what will be done while transferring a patient so that appropriate techniques will be utilised. This is because without planning you or the patient may acquire an injury.</li>
<li>Explain to the patient what will be done. Then use the patients ability to assist as much as possible to reduce the workload on you, the nurse.</li>
<li>Remove obstacles that may make transferring more difficult prior to transferral.</li>
<li>Elevate the patient's bed as necessary so that work is being done at a safe and comfortable level.</li>
<li>Lock the wheels of the bed, wheelchair or stretcher to prevent them from sliding as the patient is moved</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="basic-guidelines-when-transferring-a-patient">Basic Guidelines when Transferring a Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-guidelines-when-transferring-a-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Observe sound principles of body mechanics so that muscles are not strained and injured.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Be sure to keep the patients in proper alignment during transfer procedures so that the patient is also protected from strain and muscle injury.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Support the patient's body, especially near the joints. Avoid grabbing and holding extremely by the muscles, which will injure tissues and often put unnecessary strain on joints.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid causing friction on the patient's skin. Roll or push the patient when possible rather than pull them across bed linens. Friction can be reduced by sprinkling powder or cornstarch on the patient's skin and linens.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use smooth rather than jerky movements when transferring the patient. Jerky motion tends to put extra strain on muscles and joints and is uncomfortable for the patient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Be realistic about how much you can safely do without injury</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="transferring-a-patient-to-and-from-a-stretcher">Transferring a Patient To and From a Stretcher<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transferring-a-patient-to-and-from-a-stretcher" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You must take great care, when transferring a helpless patient, to prevent injuring the patient and yourself.</p>
<p>The extremities and the head must be supported well. The most convenient way to move a patient is to place a sheet underneath them, then pull carefully on the sheet under the patient to another point, such as from a bed to a stretcher and from a stretcher back to a bed.</p>
<p>When a patient must be lifted and carried, a three-carrier lift is recommended.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-ed584ffb.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="transferring-a-patient-from-a-bed-to-a-chair-and-back-to-bed">Transferring a Patient From a Bed to a Chair and Back to Bed<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transferring-a-patient-from-a-bed-to-a-chair-and-back-to-bed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The chair in which a patient sits should make it possible for them to maintain good posture. If a patient can assist and stand while they are being transferred from a bed to a chair or wheelchair, use the following techniques:</p>
<ul>
<li>Use equipment with firm and stable surfaces. If the mattress is soft and the patient sinks into it, place a bed board under it before transferring the patient to a chair or wheelchair</li>
<li>Take the patient's condition into account</li>
<li>Make distance for transferring as short as possible</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Place the chair or wheel chair parallel to and near to the head of the bed. Be sure that the wheels of a wheelchair are locked and the foot supports are in the upright position.</li>
<li>Place the short bed rails in the up position so that the patient can grasp a rail to sit up in bed and steady their self as they move.</li>
<li>Stand on the side of the bed on which the patient will be moving. Do not reach across the bed to assist the patient. Help the patient to a sitting position.</li>
<li>Allow the patient to sit a few seconds until you are sure they are not feeling faint.</li>
<li>Pivot the patient appropriately as they sit at the side of the bed. If they are going to walk, help them put on shoes and stockings. Hard soled and well fitting shoes will give them more support than loose, floppy slippers.</li>
<li>Place the bed in the low position or have a foot-stool handy on which the patient can stand on as they get out of bed.</li>
<li>Face the patient, spread their feet to provide a wide base of support and balance, put one of your feet forward between the patient's feet, and flex the knees to provide stability. The patient puts their hands on your shoulders, while you hold in the ancillary area. Grasping the patient on their chest wall is uncomfortable and restricts breathing.</li>
</ul>
<p>Some nurses prefer to lock arms to assist the patient to a standing position. This entails the following procedure:</p>
<ul>
<li>As the patient's upper body is lifted, ask the patient to lift their self from the bed. If a footstool is used, assist the patient off of it while continuing to hold them.</li>
<li>Maintain a wide base of support while pivoting with the patient so that their back is towards the chair.</li>
<li>Bend the knees and keep the back straight as the patient is lowered into the chair or wheel chair.</li>
</ul>
<p>After helping the patient to their feet, you should assist them into their chair. A chair with arms would provide another means for the patient to help support and guide them into the chair.</p>
<p>Have the patient assist by holding onto the armrests of the chair or wheelchair if they are available as they are being lowered onto it.</p>
<p>When a patient cannot assist with the transfer, for example, a patient cannot stand before they sit in a chair, it is best to have two persons lift the patient from the bed into a chair. One person can do so unless the patient is too heavy.</p>
<p>The single person technique is handy for home use and in situations when only one person is available. With the chair near the bed, and while supporting the patient from the back, gently move the helpless patient into the chair.</p>
<p>You should have a wide base of support. Bend your knees and rock back as the patient slides to the chair. Place the patient's feet and legs onto the bed first as you roll them off the chair and onto the bed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="collection-of-specimens">Collection of Specimens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#collection-of-specimens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are conversant with most of the procedures involved in the collection of specimens from patients because you have been performing these procedures. You may have assisted a doctor or clinical officer in the collection of specimens.</p>
<p>You have already studied infection prevention and control. During these procedures you will be dealing with body fluids and sharps. You therefore need to apply the knowledge you have acquired on infection prevention to be able to protect yourself, the patient and coworkers.</p>
<p>You also need to recall the body structures where the body fluids will be collected from and your knowledge of microbiology. You should not only know the techniques of collecting the specimens but also the interpretation of the findings. The specimens you will study include: blood, urine, stool, swabs and sputum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blood-collection">Blood Collection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blood-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The indications for the collection of blood specimen include: anaemia, infective conditions e.g. septicaemia, severe haemorrhage and so on.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="think-about-what-you-require-for-the-collection-of-blood-specimens">Think about what you require for the collection of blood specimens?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#think-about-what-you-require-for-the-collection-of-blood-specimens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A nurse should have a tray containing:</p>
<ul>
<li>Disposable syringes and needles</li>
<li>Sterile swabs and spirits swabs in separate containers</li>
<li>A receiver for used swabs</li>
<li>A rubber tourniquet</li>
<li>Assorted specimen containers</li>
<li>Strapping</li>
<li>A pair of scissors</li>
<li>Laboratory request forms</li>
<li>Container for sharps</li>
<li>Gloves</li>
<li>Two blood slides</li>
<li>Lancet/needle, which is sterile</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>The collection procedure will vary, depending on the type of investigation required. Whatever the case, you will need to prepare the patient, environment, equipment and yourself. The following preparations need to be undertaken</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patient">Patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Explain the procedure to the patient and put them in a comfortable position.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environment">Environment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Screen the bed. Ensure adequate working place.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="equipment">Equipment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#equipment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wash the tray with soapy water, rinse and dry. Clean with antiseptic swab. Arrange the equipment neatly on the tray and take to the bedside. Label specimen bottles and slides.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nurse">Nurse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nurse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Wash your hands and put on gloves.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-of-sample-collection">Method of Sample Collection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-of-sample-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following is standard procedure when collecting blood samples from a patient:</p>
<ol>
<li>Identify the site</li>
<li>Apply the tourniquet</li>
<li>Decontaminate the skin at the site of puncture</li>
<li>Identify the vein</li>
<li>Introduce the needle and withdraw the required amount of blood</li>
<li>Release tourniquet</li>
<li>Withdraw needle</li>
<li>Apply pressure to the puncture site immediately after the needle is withdrawn using a sterile dry swab</li>
<li>Put blood in correct specimen container</li>
<li>Put syringe and needle in sharps container</li>
<li>Ensure bottles are labelled correctly</li>
<li>Leave the patient comfortable</li>
<li>Send to the laboratory immediately with appropriate request form</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blood-slide-for-malaria-parasites">Blood Slide for Malaria Parasites<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blood-slide-for-malaria-parasites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following method is suitable for use when analysing for the presence of malarial parasites:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Clean the patient's middle finger with spirit swab.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pinch finger below puncture site and prick once with lancet or needle steadily.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wipe off the first drop of blood using a dry sterile swab.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Squeeze and receive the next drop onto the blood slide and set aside.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Squeeze the third drop and ask patient to smear this drop onto the second slide using the pricked finger.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask the patient to apply pressure to the punctured site using a dry sterile swab.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Allow blood to dry on slide.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Leave patient comfortable.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Take slides to laboratory with request forms.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clearing">Clearing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When clearing, do not forget to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Remove screens</li>
<li>Discard disposable equipment</li>
<li>Clean the tray and keep it in its place</li>
<li>Decontaminate equipment, wash with soapy water, rinse, dry and store appropriately</li>
<li>Wash hands</li>
<li>Record, interpret and report findings</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="urine-collection">Urine Collection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urine-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Urine is taken to analyse for diagnostic purpose. Urine collection is used to indicate infective conditions and to confirm pregnancy. The requirements for effective urine analysis include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Appropriate specimen container</li>
<li>Request form</li>
<li>A measuring jug</li>
<li>Spirit swabs in container</li>
<li>Sterile syringe and needle</li>
<li>Urine bag to collect specimen from babies and small children</li>
<li>Gloves</li>
<li>Toilet paper</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following steps should be followed when undertaking urine analysis:</p>
<ol>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient</li>
<li>Ensure privacy</li>
<li>Assemble required equipment</li>
<li>Obtain specimen bottles and label</li>
<li>Wash your hands and put on gloves if necessary</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="routine-urine-specimen">Routine Urine Specimen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#routine-urine-specimen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following should be taken into consideration when collecting the urine specimen:</p>
<ul>
<li>If a patient is able to give specimen independently, instruct them to pass urine directly into the container.</li>
<li>If patient requires assistance, give a clean bed pan/ urinal/ or in the case of infants, apply bag.</li>
<li>Instruct the patient not to pass faeces into the bed pan.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Pour the clean specimen into the specimen bottle.</li>
<li>If the patient has an in dwelling catheter, allow urine to collect in bladder for approximately 30 minutes.</li>
<li>Disconnect the catheter from urine bag, maintaining asepsis.</li>
<li>Release clamps and allow urine to flow into the container.</li>
<li>Test urine in the ward or take immediately to the laboratory with request form.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="midstream-urine-specimen-for-culture-and-sensitivity">Midstream Urine Specimen for Culture and Sensitivity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#midstream-urine-specimen-for-culture-and-sensitivity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If a patient is able to give specimen independently, instruct them as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Open specimen bottle carefully without touching the inside of bottle or lid.</li>
<li>Wash genital area with soapy water, rinse and dry.</li>
<li>Pass the first flow into the toilet, urinal or bedpan, the middle flow into the container and last flow into the toilet, urinal or bedpan.</li>
<li>If the patient should require assistance, follow the above procedure except that you should clean the patient's genital area and/or apply a urine bag in the case of an infant.</li>
<li>If the patient has an in dwelling catheter, allow urine to collect in bladder.</li>
<li>Using the aseptic technique, swab the outside of the distal end of catheter, insert a sterile needle and, with the syringe still attached to the needle, aspirate the required amount of urine.</li>
<li>Put urine into sterile specimen bottle.</li>
<li>If catheterization is inevitable to obtain the specimen, follow catheterization procedure.</li>
<li>Take specimen immediately to laboratory with request form.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="24-hour-urine-specimen">24-hour Urine Specimen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#24-hour-urine-specimen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Urine collection should start between 6 a.m. to 8 a.m. so that the specimen can be taken to the laboratory during early working hours. The following procedure should be adhered to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Give the patient a jug to void into.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Instruct patient to collect all urine for 24-hour period.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At the starting time, instruct patient to void and discard this urine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All urine subsequently passed, including the last voiding, is collected in the bottle for 24 hours.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Take to laboratory immediately with request form.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decontaminate the urine jug. Wash with soapy water, rinse, dry and store appropriately.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash your hands thoroughly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Record, interpret and report findings.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="swab-specimens">Swab Specimens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#swab-specimens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following equipment is required when collecting swab specimens. You should have a tray containing:</p>
<ul>
<li>Container with culture medium if required</li>
<li>Sterile swab</li>
<li>Wooden spatula</li>
<li>Torch</li>
<li>Request form</li>
<li>Normal saline in gallipots</li>
<li>Slides</li>
<li>Gloves</li>
<li>Masks if necessary</li>
<li>Sterile dressing pack if necessary</li>
