<li>Sterile speculum in kidney dish</li>
<li>Warm water in a bowl</li>
<li>Gauze swabs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The first step is preparation.</p>
<p>For this you must:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient</li>
<li>Put the patient in appropriate position</li>
<li>Screen the bed</li>
<li>Ensure adequate working space</li>
<li>Assemble the required equipment and take to bedside</li>
<li>Label specimen container</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The method for collection of swabs differs according to the type of specimen being collected.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="throat-swab">Throat Swab<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#throat-swab" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When taking a throat swab, the following procedure should be adhered to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ask the patient to open mouth wide and put tongue out.</li>
<li>Depress the tongue lightly with spatula. Direct the light to the back of the throat and ask patient to say "A, A, A".</li>
<li>Gently but firmly sweep over inflamed area, taking care not to touch the tongue with swab.</li>
<li>Immediately put swab in container with medium using a septic technique.</li>
<li>Take to laboratory immediately with request form.</li>
<li>Leave patient comfortable.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 51 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="wound-swab">Wound Swab<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wound-swab" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When taking a wound swab you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Remove dressing if necessary. Observe the condition of the wound and determine the appropriate site for taking specimen such as infected area or pus.</li>
<li>Gently but firmly sweep over the inflamed area once with sterile swab, making sure swab is well soaked with drainage.</li>
<li>Immediately put swab in container with medium using a septic technique.</li>
<li>Take immediately to laboratory with request form.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="wound-swab">Wound Swab<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wound-swab" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When taking a wound swab you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Remove dressing if necessary. Observe the condition of the wound and determine the appropriate site for taking specimen such as infected area or pus.</li>
<li>Gently but firmly sweep over the inflamed area once with sterile swab, making sure swab is well soaked with drainage.</li>
<li>Immediately put swab in container with medium using a septic technique.</li>
<li>Take immediately to laboratory with request form.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="high-vagina-swab">High Vagina Swab<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#high-vagina-swab" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following procedure should be followed when taking a high vagina swab:</p>
<ul>
<li>Request the patient to empty bladder, clean and dry the vulva with warm water using cotton swabs.</li>
<li>Encourage the patient to breathe deeply for ease of insertion.</li>
<li>Lubricate the speculum with sterile warm water.</li>
<li>Insert the speculum gently and open it to expose the cervix.</li>
<li>Direct light to cervical area.</li>
<li>Gently but firmly sweep the high fornix area once, and put the swab into the container with medium.</li>
<li>Remove the speculum gently and put in kidney dish for decontamination.</li>
<li>Leave the patient comfortable.</li>
<li>Immediately take specimen to laboratory with request form.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clearing">Clearing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>After swabbing, the following clearing procedures should be adhered to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Remove screens</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Discard disposable items</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decontaminate equipment, wash with soapy water, rinse, dry and store appropriately</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Record, interpret and report findings</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sputum-collection">Sputum Collection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sputum-collection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A sputum specimen is collected to analyse for diagnostic purposes. If the specimen is for culture and sensitivity, it should be collected using septic technique. In children a gastric lavage is performed.</p>
<p>As a nurse, you should emphasise the importance of obtaining an early morning specimen, prior to cleaning the mouth or eating. Instruct the patient to cough deeply so that secretion comes from the lungs and is not simply saliva from the mouth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="requirements">Requirements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following items are required when collecting a sputum specimen:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mouth wash</li>
<li>A sputum mug</li>
<li>Appropriate specimen container</li>
<li>Request forms</li>
<li>Gloves</li>
<li>Mask, if necessary</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During the preparation phase, the following should be remembered:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient.</li>
<li>Screen bed if necessary.</li>
<li>Assemble required equipment and take to the bedside.</li>
<li>Label specimen container.</li>
<li>Wash your hands and wear gloves if necessary.</li>
<li>Instruct the patient on what to do and how to deposit the sputum into the specimen container.</li>
<li>Take to the laboratory immediately.</li>
<li>Offer patient mouthwash.</li>
<li>Leave the patient comfortable.</li>
</ul>
<p>After the specimen has been collected, the following clearing procedures are necessary:</p>
<ul>
<li>Decontaminate, wash with soapy water, rinse, dry and store appropriately.</li>
<li>Offer patient sputum mug when necessary.</li>
<li>Record, interpret and report findings.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="neurological-observations">Neurological Observations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurological-observations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Neurological observations are done to monitor the progress of a patient with suspected or confirmed injury to the nervous system or to</p>
<p>investigate the efficiency of the nervous system. These observations are indicated in unconsciousness, head injury following neurosurgery and poisoning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="requirements">Requirements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are required when undertaking a neurological examination. In addition to the neurological chart, you must have a tray containing:</p>
<ul>
<li>Torch with batteries</li>
<li>Thermometers in lotion and swabs in gallipot</li>
<li>Sphygmomanometer</li>
<li>Stethoscope</li>
<li>Receiver for dirty swabs</li>
<li>Sterile pins (for pricking)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Prepare the patient. This should be done in the following manner:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ensure that the patient is comfortable and appropriately positioned.</li>
<li>Screen the bed if necessary.</li>
<li>Darken the room if necessary.</li>
<li>Clean and dry the tray and then arrange the equipment on it neatly.</li>
<li>Get the neurological chart or draw up one if not available.</li>
<li>Place the tray and chart next to the patient on the locker.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following method should be adhered to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Call the patient by name. If there is no answer, give a command e.g. 'open your eyes' or 'close your eyes'.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is no response, record appropriately.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is no response, press firmly the angle of the jaw below the ear using thumb or prick lightly with a sterile pin and observe facial expression.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Record under response to stimuli as 'responding well' or 'not well'.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is no response, or poor response, record under level of consciousness column as 'deeply unconscious' or 'semi-conscious'.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To determine muscle tone and strength, ask the patient to grasp and squeeze your hands and compare the strength of each hand.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask the patient to bend their knees and push feet against your palms and compare response and strength.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open both eyes and note size and shape of each pupil. Also check if both pupils are equal in size and whether they react to light equally.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open the left eye by raising the upper eyelid and shine the torch from lateral side towards the middle of the eye and note the pupil reaction to light. Wait for a few seconds, repeat the process and note reactions. Record response to light of left eye under 'L', if dilated or constricted and reacting or not reacting or sluggish reaction to light as applicable.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Repeat the process for right eye and record under 'R'.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Take the vital observations and record under appropriate headings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Note and report any change in all observations (it is important to report promptly) to include volume of pulse, depth and regularity of breathing, temporary cessation of breathing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continue with these observations <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>4</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{1}{4}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">4</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">â€‹</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{1}{2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">â€‹</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> hourly or as indicated by the doctor.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Keep the patient comfortable.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clearing">Clearing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Clear as necessary, following the basic procedures outlined previously and then record, interpret and report findings.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-a8c55359.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="administration-of-drugs">Administration of Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#administration-of-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Drug administration should be performed systematically and carefully to ensure that the right patient is given the correct prescribed drugs and dose and at the right time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="oral-route">Oral route<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oral-route" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Take Medicine Orally procedure is indicated in the treatment of disease/conditions whereby a patient is able to swallow.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 52 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 53 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="requirements">Requirements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following should be kept in mind in relation to the administration of drugs. On the top shelf ensure there is the following items:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drugs in use in a tray with labels facing the front</li>
<li>Medicine measures</li>
<li>Spoons for capsules tablets/pills</li>
<li>Special spoon for liquid drugs</li>
<li>Small plates or saucers x 2</li>
<li>Medicine cloth x 1</li>
<li>Clean, plain paper for crushing tablets</li>
<li>Hand towel</li>
<li>Damp bottle cloth</li>
<li>A paper for recording antibiotics and missing drugs</li>
<li>Milk in a jar or packets for special patients</li>
</ul>
<p>On the bottom shelf ensure there is:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drinking water in a jar</li>
<li>A bowl of warm soapy water for cleaning spoons and measures</li>
<li>A tray containing syringes and kidney dish, a gallipot with water or blue litmus paper (if required for drugs administered through a nasal gastric tube)</li>
<li>A receiver for contaminated items</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preparation">Preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During the preparation phase, you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient</li>
<li>Ask the patient if they have any allergies</li>
<li>Ensure all patients are in their right beds and ready</li>
<li>Ensure the environment is conducive to safe drug administration</li>
<li>Clean the trolley and dry it</li>
<li>Wipe the medicine measures, spoons, bowls and plates then place them on the trolley</li>
<li>Place a clean piece of paper on the trolley under the plates</li>
<li>Prepare the paper for recording antibiotics and any other relevant information</li>
<li>Put cold water in the jar and place on the trolley</li>
<li>Put warm water in two bowls and prepare the soapy water</li>
<li>Arrange the commonly used drugs on the tray</li>
<li>Check with the ward in charge for any labels that are not clear or any spoilt labels</li>
<li>Close and lock the medicine cupboard and put the keys in your pocket</li>
</ul>
<p>If you have any patient on drugs through a nasal gastric tube, make the tray for this ready before preparing your medicine trolley. You must have a pen and a watch ready at all times.</p>
<p>It is safer for the nasal gastric tube procedure to be conducted by two nurses. In case of students, a qualified nurse should guide them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When administering drugs, the following methods should be adhered to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Wash your hands and dry them</li>
<li>Wheel the trolley and begin from one end of the ward</li>
<li>Take the treatment sheet, read the patient's name and confirm by asking/calling patient's name to ensure that they are the right patient in the right bed</li>
<li>Check on drug allergies</li>
<li>Read the whole treatment sheet noting the drugs that are due to be given, according to the date and time</li>
<li>Read the prescription against the containers, checking with the second nurse, and note the dosages on the prescription and on the container</li>
<li>If mixtures, shake the bottle gently by turning up and down until the drug is well mixed</li>
<li>Make sure the label on the bottle is uppermost to avoid soiling the label</li>
<li>Remove the cork/cap and pour the drug in the medicine measure or spoon</li>
<li>Measure the dose at the eye level when using the measuring container</li>
<li>Replace the cork cap</li>
<li>If a patient is getting more than one mixture use separate container for each mixture</li>
<li>If tablets, put the needed tablets into a spoon, put spoon on a saucer</li>
<li>Take medicine to the patient</li>
<li>Check the dose, date and time against the prescription before giving it to the patient</li>
<li>Confirm the right patient by name before giving the medicine</li>
<li>Make sure the patient swallows the medicine in your presence</li>
<li>Give a drink of water, milk or juice</li>
<li>Record all the antibiotics and other drugs in the patient's notes as you give them</li>
</ul>
<p>Never leave the medication trolley unattended!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clearing">Clearing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When clearing, make sure the following procedures are carried out:</p>
<ul>
<li>Wheel the trolley to the duty room</li>
<li>Wipe all the bottles and make sure all containers have their lids well secured</li>
<li>Clean the spoons, bowls, medicine measures and dry them before returning them to the cupboards</li>
<li>Replace the drugs tidily in the cupboards</li>
<li>Wipe the trolley and leave in the correct place</li>
<li>Clean the medicine cloth if dirty</li>
<li>Record all the antibiotics in the antibiotic register and any other special drugs in the care index</li>
<li>Report any missing drugs and important observations of the patients' conditions to the ward in charge</li>
<li>Record, interpret and report findings, for example, if drug vomited, drug refused, drug reaction, general condition of patient and so on</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="injections">Injections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#injections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several types of injections, that is: intramuscular, hypodermic/subcutaneous and intradermal. Each of these will be covered in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intramuscular">Intramuscular<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intramuscular" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This injection can be administered on several sites.</p>
<p>These include: the upper outer quadrant of the buttock (deep into the muscles); anterior lateral aspect of the thigh and the deltoid muscle in selected cases.</p>
<p>The method of injection involves holding the needle at an angle of 90 degrees to the skin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypodermic-subcutaneous">Hypodermic/Subcutaneous<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypodermic-subcutaneous" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This injection can be administered on the upper outer arm or thigh (into the connective tissue) or in the abdominal wall.</p>
<p>The needle should be held at an angle of 45 degrees to the skin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intradermal">Intradermal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intradermal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An intradermal injection is performed on the dorsum of the forearm. The injected fluid raises a wheal. This is used mainly for BCG, Mantoux test or drug test doses. Stretch the area of the skin between the thumb and finger.</p>
<p>Introduce the needle into the skin keeping it parallel to the skin at 10-15 degrees angle. Do not massage the area after removing the needle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-requirements-for-giving-injections">General Requirements for Giving Injections<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-requirements-for-giving-injections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When giving injections ensure that the following are to be found on the top shelf of the trolley:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drugs to be used in a container</li>
<li>A file</li>
<li>Sterile water for injection</li>
<li>Spirit swabs in a bowl</li>
<li>Disposable sterile syringes and needles in a container</li>
<li>Receiver for carrying the drug to the bedside</li>
<li>Paper and pen for relevant information</li>
</ul>
<p>And on the bottom shelf of trolley:</p>
<ul>
<li>Receiver for used swabs</li>
<li>Well labelled sharps container for used syringes, needles and ampoules</li>
<li>Container for vials</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation">Preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When preparing the patient for the procedure, please ensure that you undertake the following steps:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient</li>
<li>Check for allergies</li>
<li>Screen the bed if necessary</li>
<li>If a trolley is not in use, prepare a locker for tray storage</li>
<li>Make the injection list from the patients note</li>
<li>Wash hands and clean the trolley</li>
<li>Clean the tray and disinfect it with spirit swabs</li>
<li>Assemble equipment on the trolley</li>
<li>Place the tray on the trolley and place the sterile equipment on the top shelf</li>
<li>Put the un-sterile equipment, injection list and rough paper on the top shelf at the side</li>
<li>Two nurses should work together</li>
</ul>
<p>This is a sterile procedure as you studied in section one of this unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method">Method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following general method should be followed:</p>
<ul>
<li>Take the ampoule or vial of the prescribed drug from the locked cupboard</li>
<li>Check the name, dose of the drug and the name of the patient against the prescription</li>
<li>Wash hands, dry them on a clean towel and put on gloves</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Pour a little antiseptic over one of the swabs to be used in order to clean the skin area of the injection</li>
<li>If using ampoules, file the neck then, protecting the fingers with a cotton wool swab, break the ampoule off the neck</li>
<li>If using a vial, remove the metal cap, use spirit swab to clean the top</li>
<li>Dilute the drug with the correct amount of water and mix well</li>
<li>Draw up the drug into the syringe, then using a cotton wool swab placed at the neck of the syringe, hold up and eject any air which might have entered the syringe. This prevents any spray of drug from contaminating your hands and face</li>
<li>Remove used needle and discard in sharps container and replace with new needle, place in sterile container (e.g. kidney dish, paper bag) and place on tray</li>
<li>Take trolley/tray to the bedside</li>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient a second time and ask them not to move while you are giving the injection</li>
<li>Check the name, the dose of the drug and the names of the patient again at the bedside, care must be taken if there are two patients in the ward bearing the same names</li>
<li>Locate the injection site and clean it with the spirit swab</li>
<li>Hold the skin between the fore fingers and thumb and insert the needle</li>
<li>Withdraw the piston slightly to ensure that the point of the needle has not entered a blood vessel, if blood is seen discard medication and equipment and prepare again</li>
<li>If all is well, push the drug in and with the swab placed over the needle withdraw quickly</li>
<li>Give a little massage to aid in absorption of the drug</li>
<li>Immediately discard needle and syringe into sharps container</li>
</ul>
<p>Always use an injection list to guide you on what drugs to remove from the cupboard!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clearing">Clearing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>After giving the injection it is important to ensure that proper clearing takes place. For this reason, you should:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Tidy the patient's bed and leave them comfortable</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Remove the screens to their appropriate place</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Take the trolley or tray to the duty room and clean with soap and water</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Discard swabs in the dustbin and leave the room tidy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Record the antibiotics in the antibiotic register or any other drugs in the care index and in the patient's notes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Remove gloves and dispose as appropriate. Wash hands with soap and water and dry them</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Do not leave the medicine trolley or tray unattended. The drug cupboard should be kept locked and keys kept in the pocket of the one administering drugs.</p>
<p>Finally, record, interpret and report findings.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="monitoring-intravenous-fluids">Monitoring Intravenous Fluids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monitoring-intravenous-fluids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Intravenous fluids are those solutions instilled within the patient's vein. They may include solutions of water and chemicals normally found within the body, dissolved medications or blood, blood extracts and blood substitutes.</p>
<p>You will be expected at times to administer and regulate intravenous fluids.</p>
<p>You will also be assigned to care for patients receiving parenteral fluids thereby monitoring the infusion, observing the patient and discontinuing the therapy as necessary</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-five-indications-for-administering-intravenous-fluids">List five indications for administering intravenous fluids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-five-indications-for-administering-intravenous-fluids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To restore fluid balance quickly when a patient experiences a significant fluid loss</li>
<li>To prevent fluid imbalance for a patient who is currently or potentially likely to experience a loss of body fluid</li>
<li>To maintain fluid balance when the patient temporarily is unable to eat and drink</li>
<li>To replace specific electrolytes or other chemicals such as water soluble vitamins</li>
<li>To provide some measure of nutrition</li>
<li>To administer medications</li>
<li>To replace blood cells or specific components of blood</li>
</ul>
<p>You must exercise extreme caution to ensure that the correct solution is infused, because any substance that is instilled directly into the circulatory system produces a rapid effect due to its almost instant distribution throughout the body.</p>
<p>There are two categories of intravenous fluids: crystalloid or colloid solutions.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 55 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Crystalloid Solutions</p>
<p>Crystalloid solutions are a mixture of water and salt or sugar. They can be further sub-divided into isotonic, hypotonic and hypertonic solutions.</p>
<p>An isotonic solution contains an equal amount of dissolved crystals as normally found in plasma.</p>
<p>A hypotonic solution contains fewer dissolved crystals than are normally found in plasma. It presents as a dilute solution in comparison to the fluid within and around cells.</p>
<p>A hypertonic solution has a higher amount of dissolved crystals than present in plasma. It will draw water into the intravascular compartment from the more dilute areas of water within the cells and interstitial spaces.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Solution</th><th>Components</th><th>Specific Comments</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Isotonic solutions 0.9 % saline (normal saline) 5 % dextrose and water (DW). Ringer's solution or lactated Ringer's.</td><td>0.9 of sodium chloride per 100 ml water 5 g of dextrose (glucose/sugar) in each 100 ml of water. Water and mixture of sodium chloride, calcium, potassium, Bicarbonate and in some cases lactate.</td><td>Contains an amount of sodium and chloride physiologically equal to that found in plasma. Isotonic when infused but the glucose is metabolised quickly, leaving a solution of dilute water. Replaces electrolytes in amounts similarly found in plasma. The lactate, when present, helps maintain acid base balance.</td></tr><tr><td>Hypotonic solutions 0.45 % sodium chloride (Half strength saline) 5 % dextrose in 0.45 saline.</td><td>0.45 g of sodium chloride in each 10 ml of water. 5 g of dextrose and 0.45 &amp; sodium chloride per 100 ml of water.</td><td>A smaller ratio of sodium and chloride than found in plasma causing it to be less concentrated in comparison. The sugar provides a quick source ion energy, leaving a hypotonic salt solution.</td></tr><tr><td>Hypertonic solutions 10 % dextrose in water (Diolw) 3 % saline</td><td>10 g of dextrose per 100 ml of water. 3 g of sodium chloride per 100 ml of water.</td><td>Twice the concentration of glucose than present in plasma. The high concentration of salt in the plasma will dehydrate cells and tissue.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Check your medicine cupboard. What do you find on the bottom shelf?</p>
<p>Normally nursing units stock commonly used intravenous solutions in utility rooms or medication cupboards.</p>
<p>Blood and blood products are stored in the blood bank.</p>
<p>The preparation of solutions and equipment requires adherence to principles of asepsis. You should therefore practice good hand washing technique, and skills that will prevent contamination of any openings, or equipment that could introduce organisms into the patients' circulatory system.</p>
<p>Performing Vein Punctures</p>
<p>You will become skilled in performing vein punctures with continued practice and experience, especially with relation to site selection and insertion.</p>
<p>Selecting a Vein</p>
<p>The choice of the site of a vein puncture varies with each patient.</p>
<p>While selecting a vein you should consider the following factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>Superficial veins are easily located and are more accessible for puncture.</li>
<li>Veins in the arm and hands are preferred to veins in the foot or leg.</li>
<li>Use veins in the arm or hand on the patient's non-dominant site.</li>
<li>At times, the choices available for possible sites may be limited by the patient's condition, for example, in cases of severe burns of both arms.</li>
<li>Avoid using an area of a vein that will compromise joint movement.</li>
<li>Distend and inspect the veins. It is best to select a vein as low as possible on the back of the hand or on the lower forearm.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 56 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>If the vein is damaged, another vein higher on the arm can be used subsequently.</p>
<ul>
<li>Feel and look for an area in the vein that is fairly straight.</li>
<li>Avoid thin walled and scarred veins. They are difficult to enter. A normal vein is smooth, pliable and resilient.</li>
<li>Do not insert a needle into a valve in the vein.</li>
<li>Use larger veins for infusing hypertonic solutions, those containing irritant medications, those administered rapidly and those that are thick or sticky.</li>
<li>These should be infused in the forearm.</li>
<li>Spare sites that may be needed for subsequent infusions. If the duration of fluid is likely to be lengthy change sites periodically.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="calculating-the-infusion-rate">Calculating the Infusion Rate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calculating-the-infusion-rate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is your responsibility to calculate, regulate and maintain the rate of flow according to prescription. The prescription indicates the number of millilitres to be given within a period of time, for example, eight or two hour periods. You should then calculate the flow on the basis of drops of solution per minute.</p>
<p>How do you determine how many millilitres of solution are to be given each hour?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="just-look-at-the-following-formula">Just look at the following formula:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#just-look-at-the-following-formula" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Total number of mls to be given</p>
<p>Hours in which the solution is to be infused</p>
<p>Here is an example scenario:</p>
<p>3000 ml of solution to be infused over a 24 hour period</p>
<p>3000ml</p>
<p>24 hours</p>
<p>= 125 ml to be infused per hour</p>
<p>= ml to be given per hr</p>
<p>You should then determine the number of drops to be infused per minute as shown below:</p>
<p>Number of ml per hour x drop factor = drops per minute</p>
<p>60 minutes</p>
<p>If 125 ml needs to be infused per hour, and the intravenous</p>
<p>equipment has a drop factor of 20 drops equal 1 ml.</p>
<p>Try to calculate how many drops need to be infused per</p>
<p>minute using the formula above</p>
<p>125 ml x 20 drops/ml = 41.67 = 42 drops per minute</p>
<p>60 min</p>
<p>You should then count the number of drops falling into the drip chamber of the tubing per minute. By adjusting the regulator clamp, the number of drops per minute will be increased or decreased until the infusion matches the rate you calculated, i.e. 42 drops per minute.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="monitoring-the-rate-of-infusion">Monitoring the Rate of Infusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monitoring-the-rate-of-infusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is important to maintain the proper rate of flow because too slow a flow may not meet the patient's needs for fluid and infusing fluid too rapidly may overburden the body's ability to adjust to increases in the fluid volume, the electrolytes or the medications that may have been added. Make timely observations at least every hour to determine that the volume of intravenous solution is infusing according to schedule. You could mark the container at points indicating the amounts that should be infusing hour by hour so that at a glance you are able to tell whether the solution is being infused at proper hourly rate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="re-adjusting-the-rate-of-flow">Re-adjusting the Rate of Flow<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#re-adjusting-the-rate-of-flow" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You may need to make necessary adjustments in the rate of flow if the infusion is not progressing according to schedule.</p>
<p>To compensate for a low or excess of infused volume, the rate should be adjusted over each remaining hour of administration. The increased or decreased rate should never exceed 25% of the original infusion rate.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example-scenario">Example Scenario<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example-scenario" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fluid is to infuse at a rate of 125 ml per hour or 42 drops per minute using the drop factor of 20 drops equal 1 ml. Two hours after hanging 1000 ml of fluid you note that only 125 ml have infused instead of the scheduled 250 ml. A total of 875 ml remain in the container.</p>
<p>You should assess the site, pulling back on the needle a bit, lowering or elevating and depressing the needle you may determine that the rate has slowed due to the level of the needle resting against the vein wall. Reposition the angle with a small piece of gauze. Recalculate the new rate of flow by using the following formula.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Millimetres of fluid remaining</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Hours of administration remaining = new volume of ml per hour</td></tr><tr><td>Try to calculate the new volume to be infused per hour using the formula above</td></tr><tr><td>875 ml = 145. 8 = 146 ml per hour</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>To determine this recalculated rate will not exceed the 25% limit, you should calculate as follows.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="step-one">Step One<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-one" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Previous volume per hour â€“ new volume per hour = ml of difference</p>
<p>Example:
146 ml per hour (new volume) â€“ 125 ml per hour (previous volume) = 21 ml difference</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="step-two">Step Two<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-two" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Millilitres difference x 100</p>
<p>Previous ml per hour = Percentage of rate change</p>
<p>21ml</p>
<p>125 ml = 0.168 x 100 = 16.8 = 17% change in infusion rate</p>
<p>Since this is within the acceptable range of safety, you may readjust the rate of flow using the previous formula for calculating the drops per minute in order to infuse the new volume.</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mn>146</mn><mo>Ã—</mo><mn>20</mn></mrow><mn>60</mn></mfrac><mo>=</mo><mn>48.67</mn><mtext>&nbsp;ml</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>49</mn><mtext>&nbsp;ml&nbsp;per&nbsp;hour&nbsp;(new&nbsp;rate)</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{146 \times 20}{60} = 48.67 \text{ ml} = 49 \text{ ml per hour (new rate)}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.0074em; vertical-align: -0.686em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.3214em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">60</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">146</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Ã—</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mord">20</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">â€‹</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord">48.67</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;ml</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">49</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;ml&nbsp;per&nbsp;hour&nbsp;(new&nbsp;rate)</span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>If the difference is greater than 25% inform the doctor of the current fluid assessment such as the patient's blood pressure, pulse, respiratory rate and current urine output. The doctor may prescribe a readjustment in the volume that can be infused.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="care-of-the-patients">Care of the Patients<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-the-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When caring for the patient after performing a vein puncture the following points should be kept in mind:</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintain personal hygiene</li>
<li>Maintain the infusion</li>
<li>Inspect and dress the vein puncture site</li>
<li>Maintain aseptic technique when changing on the dressing the vein puncture site</li>
<li>Take care when changing solution containers or infusion tubing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-do-you-detect-complications">How do you detect complications?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-do-you-detect-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Make regular assessment of the site of the infusion, the equipment that is delivering the infusion and the patient's overall responses during the fluid infusion. You should be on the alert and be prepared to take action if any signs of complications occur when a patient is receiving intravenous fluids.</p>
<p>Report immediately signs and symptoms of problems with respirations such as dyspnoea, noisy breathing and coughing. Respiratory and cardiac problems are caused by circulatory overload. This may be caused by administering too much solution too quickly in relation to a patient's ability to circulate the added volume or eliminate it through urination.</p>
<p>If you detect complications what actions should you take?</p>
<p>Think of some actions you would take having detected complications.</p>
<p>The following actions should be taken if respiratory problems are detected:</p>
<ul>
<li>Decrease the flow rate</li>
<li>Place patients in Fowler's position</li>
<li>Assess vital signs</li>
<li>Notify the doctor</li>
</ul>
<p>This is a serious complication. The infusion may have to be stopped. Check for infiltration of the solution (that is, if the solution is running into tissues) commonly caused by a dislodged needle or a needle that has penetrated the wall of the vein.</p>
<p>If this happens you will observe the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>A slow rate</li>
<li>No flow of solution</li>
<li>Swelling in the area of the vein puncture site</li>
<li>A burning sensation</li>
<li>Local pallor of the skin</li>
<li>Coldness</li>
</ul>
<p>You should take the following action:</p>
<ol>
<li>Remove the needle</li>
<li>Check for phlebitis, which may occur when a solution is irritating to the vein or the vein-puncture device remains in the same site for a prolonged period of time. This is evident by the area being red, warm, swollen and painful. The heart may slow due to localised oedema</li>
<li>Select a new site for introducing additional solution</li>
<li>Elevate the arm and place warm compresses over the area of inflammation for 20 to 30 minutes, three to four times a day for one to two days</li>
<li>Notify the doctor if the fluid contained a drug that may cause injury to tissue</li>
<li>Avoid further use of vein</li>
<li>Remove the vein-puncture device</li>
<li>Restart the infusion in the opposite arm or head</li>
<li>Apply warm compresses as described earlier</li>
</ol>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 58 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Infection of the site may occur and could spread to other parts of the body through the blood stream. Evidence of infection includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>The site may appear red and puffy</li>
<li>Purulent discharge may be present</li>
<li>The patient may have a rise in temperature and/or chills</li>
</ul>
<p>In the event of possible infection:</p>
<ul>
<li>Discontinue the infusion and notify the doctor</li>
<li>Apply aseptic technique when dressing the wound</li>
<li>Take pus swab for culture and sensitivity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="discontinuing-the-infusion">Discontinuing the Infusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#discontinuing-the-infusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Discontinue the infusion when the amount of ordered solution has been infused and no more is scheduled to follow. To discontinue the infusion:</p>
<ul>
<li>Clamp the tubing and remove the tape that held the dressing and vein-puncture device in place</li>
<li>Gently press a sterile dry gauze swab over the site of puncture</li>
<li>Remove the needle or catheter by pulling it out without hesitation following the course of the vein</li>
<li>Apply pressure to the injection site for 30 to 45 seconds while elevating the forearm. This technique helps to stop bleeding from the injection site. Apply a small sterile dry gauze swab over the dressing and secure it firmly</li>
<li>Flex and extend the arm or hand several times to help the patient regain sensation and mobility in the area where the needle was located.</li>
<li>Record the amount and the type of fluid infused during the current shift on the patient's fluid intake record.</li>
<li>Document and sign for the time of termination, the type of fluid and condition of the vein puncture site in the patient's care index.</li>
<li>Remember to also give a verbal report.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incisions-and-drainage">Incisions and Drainage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incisions-and-drainage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Incision is a clean separation of skin and tissue with smooth, even edges.</p>
<p>A drain is a hollow tube through which liquid secretions from a wound are removed. Some drains are sutured in place, while others may be prevented from slipping beneath the skin by placing a safety pin or clip on the end extending from the wound.</p>
<p>When caring for a patient with a drain you should do the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Assess the characteristics and amount of drainage.</li>
<li>Cleanse the area around a drain using principles of asepsis.</li>
<li>Remove a drain as indicated.</li>
<li>Prevent injury to the wound or displacement of any granulation tissue that may be present.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="care-for-the-terminally-ill">Care for the Terminally Ill<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-for-the-terminally-ill" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A terminal illness is one from which recovery is beyond reasonable expectations. The condition contributing to death may be a disease or the result of injury.</p>
<p>When a patient is dying, you are faced with dual responsibilities. The patient requires holistic care, while at the same time the patient's family and friends need support, because all persons who have a significant relationship with the patient are dealing with grief.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="in-your-opinion-what-is-grief">In your opinion, what is grief?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#in-your-opinion-what-is-grief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Grief encompasses the physical and emotional feelings related to separation and loss. You will deal with many aspects of the dying and grieving experiences. You will cover the unique emotional, spiritual and physical problems of the terminally ill, and approaches that are hopeful in dealing with anticipatory grief.</p>
<p>Most individuals react instinctively when they are personally involved with impending death. Some common reactions among patients, family members and health care professional include denial, avoidance and hope.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="think-of-your-own-definition-of-denial-avoidance-and-hope">Think of your own definition of denial, avoidance and hope.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#think-of-your-own-definition-of-denial-avoidance-and-hope" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Denial is a physiological technique in which an individual does not believe certain information to be true.</p>
<p>Avoidance is a technique used to separate oneself from situations that are threatening or unpleasant.</p>
<p>Hope is the ability to cling to the possibility of a positive outcome against overwhelming odds. Most individuals prefer to deal with death only when it becomes absolutely necessary to do so</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-do-you-prepare-yourself-to-provide-terminal-care">How do you prepare yourself to provide terminal care?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-do-you-prepare-yourself-to-provide-terminal-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You may have already cared for a terminally ill patient. How did you feel? What were your coping mechanisms? Personal values and attitudes are closely associated with the quality of care you provide. You will explore various</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>aspects of death and dying before being faced with the actual experience.</p>
<p>You must understand your personal feelings about death and dying before you provide terminal care. If you neglect to do so, you will avoid involvement and remain detached. The most likely result of this attitude is that the dying person and the family will feel emotionally abandoned and are left to face a very frightening situation alone as you provide care without feelings.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-do-you-think-about-death-and-dying">What do you think about death and dying?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-do-you-think-about-death-and-dying" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Go through the following questions to provoke your thinking about death and dying. Assess your personal feelings. Some good questions to ask yourself are:</p>
<ul>
<li>What is my concept of death?</li>
<li>Who or what has contributed to my feelings about death?</li>
<li>What experiences are especially important to me before I die?</li>
<li>Would I want to know that my condition is terminal?</li>
<li>If I could control the events that lead to my death what would I want them to be?</li>
<li>Whom would I want to be present during my terminal illness?</li>
<li>Where would I prefer to die?</li>
<li>What fears do I have about death?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="developing-a-support-system">Developing a Support System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#developing-a-support-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should not feel that the burden of care depends solely on you. Other healthy team members may complement and supplement the nursing care of the terminally ill patient and their family. When you feel a sense of support you are in a better position to support others.</p>
<p>A support system among peers begins by developing an environment, within which nurses working together know that they can turn to each other. Peer support works best not only when you reach out for the support you need but also recognise when your peers need help and can readily say, "How can I help you?"</p>
<p>You will find yourself dealing with ethical and legal issues when caring for a terminally ill patient, such as euthanasia, a living will, and organ donations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="euthanasia">Euthanasia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#euthanasia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Euthanasia means an easy death or mercy killing. Euthanasia is considered when death is inevitable and life-saving measures are of questionable benefit.</p>
<p>You will now look at types of euthanasia. These are classified as active and passive euthanasia.</p>
<p><strong>Passive euthanasia</strong> uses techniques that relieve pain but do not delay natural death from occurring.</p>
<p><strong>Active euthanasia</strong> is the deliberate ending of life of an individual who is suffering from an incurable condition. This latter form of euthanasia is illegal.</p>
<p>No matter how hopeless the situation is, the patient and their family must remain the focus of attention. They need medical care. Remember, they need time to work through their feelings. There is need for providing quality care and dignity to the dying patient's life. Effective communication must be central to all decisions. When a Do Not Resuscitate (DNR) order has been given, you should ensure that the following is done:</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient and their family must understand the terminal nature of the condition.</li>
<li>The patient and their family should receive explanations of the possible alternatives for treatment and the options that are available.</li>
<li>Some notation about the discussion with the patient or family should be documented in the progress notes.</li>
<li>The patient should make the final decision if they are rational and capable of doing so.</li>
<li>The family members should all be involved in the decision, substituting their judgement for what they believe would be the wishes of the patient, should the patient not be capable of making a decision.</li>
<li>The order must be written on the patient's permanent record. A verbal order or a telephone order is not sufficient.</li>
<li>The order should be reviewed periodically and changed at any time the patient or the family so decides.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-living-will">A Living Will<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-living-will" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A living will is a written statement describing the wishes of a person concerning their medical care when their death is near. The written document helps guide the family and health workers to understand and implement an individual's wishes if they are unable to participate in the decision making process.</p>
<p>A living will may specify the desire for life sustaining measures or opposition to these. It generally describes a desire to avoid being</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>kept alive by artificial means or use of heroic measures when the patient is terminally ill and when there is no reasonable expectation of recovery. You are advised to follow the doctors' orders and the laws of the country when using life-prolonging measures for a terminally ill.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="organ-donation">Organ Donation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organ-donation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Body organs and tissues such as kidneys, heart, liver, pancreas, corneas, lungs and skin may be needed for transplants. Donations must be voluntarily given. Prior to death patients may grant such permission. After death, the next of the kin must sign a permit before tissue or organs may be removed from the body. Should you find yourself involved in asking terminally ill patients or their families about eventual donation of organs, you must be sensitive, compassionate and articulate. Keep these points in mind:</p>
<ul>
<li>No one should feel that another patient is being favoured at the expense of the donor.</li>
<li>Those approached as potential donors may feel victimised and extremely distraught.</li>
<li>Care must be taken that these individuals are not coerced into agreeing to organ donations or made to feel guilty for refusing.</li>
</ul>
<p>You should get acquainted with the laws and policies concerning organ donations.</p>
