<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environment">Environment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When you are exploring the environment, you are to look at it in broad perspective. Question the patient about their physical environment. The information will include the type of housing, its location, safety and comfort within the home and the neighbourhood. What you will be trying to identify are things like environmental hazards such as isolation, inadequate protection, potential risks, pollution (noise, air, water) and inadequate sanitation facilities.</p>
<p>Also discuss the spiritual environment. Spirituality is expressed through identification with a particular religion. Spiritual values and beliefs direct a person's behaviour and his approach to health problems and the health care system in general. During an illness a person faces challenges toward spirituality. You should, therefore, conduct a brief assessment of the extent to which religion is a part of the patient's life, religious beliefs related to the person's perception of health and illness and religious practices.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environment">Environment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Finally, examine the interpersonal environment, which includes cultural influences, relationships with family and friends and so on. The presence or absence of a support system is all part of the interpersonal environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ethnic-background">Ethnic Background<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ethnic-background" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Beliefs and practices that have been shared from generation to generation are known as cultural or ethnic patterns. They are expressed through language, dress, dietary choices and role behaviours and can influence perceptions of health and illness, and health related behaviour.</p>
<p>Beliefs and customs also influence the patient's experience with a health problem and their relationship with the health care team. You should, therefore, obtain relevant information to this effect with regard to their background, customs or values, special health practices including any specific practices for testing illness</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="family-relationships-and-support-systems">Family Relationships and Support Systems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family-relationships-and-support-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should assess the family structure (members, age, and role), patterns of communication and the presence or absence of a support system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lifestyle-patterns-and-habits">Lifestyle (patterns and habits)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lifestyle-patterns-and-habits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When looking at life you should obtain information about health related behaviours, for example, patterns of sleep, exercise, nutrition and recreation as well as personal habits such as smoking, use of alcohol or caffeine.</p>
<p>Obtaining information about personal habits is very difficult. You are, therefore, advised to use indirect questioning such as: "Have you ever considered cutting down your alcohol intake?"</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="self-concept">Self-concept<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#self-concept" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Self-concept is the impression one has of one's self. It is a product of relevant experiences with others and is the result of other reactions to the self. The questions you may put across to the patient may be, "How do you feel about your life in general?" or "What do you expect your life to be like in future?"</p>
<p>Health concerns may threaten the way one perceives. For instance, the mental picture one has of oneself may be the result of certain medical or surgical interventions like mastectomy or colostomy, which threaten body image. You should be aware of the patient's perceptions of themselves and their body. You could ask the patient the following questions:</p>
<ul>
<li>"What would you change about yourself if you could?"</li>
<li>"Do you have any particular concerns about your body?"</li>
</ul>
<p>Sexual history is very personal. It could be easily taken as part of the genital-urinary section within the review of body systems. You should begin with general questions that take into consideration the development stage of the person, the presence or absence of intimate relationships and so on. You should first establish whether the patient is sexually active before exploring issues related to sexual identity, contraception, or the quality of sexual relationship.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stress-response">Stress Response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stress-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You may be aware that every person handles a stressful event in a manner that is intended to eliminate or minimise the stress.</p>
<p>You should, consequently, explore past coping patterns as well as perceptions of current stresses and anticipated outcomes. These will assist you to identify the person's overall ability to handle stress.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>You should also identify expectations that the person may have of their family, friends and the health care team in helping them solve their problems.</p>
<p>Following a health history, a physical examination is then performed</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physical-examination">Physical Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As previously mentioned, the physical examination is usually performed following the health history. You should perform assessments in a well-lit, warm area. Undress and drape the patient appropriately. You should only expose the area you are to examine. At all times consider the patient's physical and psychological comfort. Explain the procedures and their rationale to the patient.</p>
<p>You should always wash your hands before and after examination. You already covered this in section one when you were looking at infection prevention and control. The health history you took will provide you with a complete health profile that guides all aspects of the physical examination. It will help you to focus on body organs and systems that are of particular concern to the patient. You will perform a systematic head to toe examination as follows: skin; head and neck; thorax and lungs; breast; cardiovascular system; abdomen; rectum; genitalia; neurological system and musculoskeletal system.</p>
<p>In your nursing practice you must have realised that you have been assessing all relevant organs during physical examination but not necessarily in the order stated above. This may be attributed to the fact that while examining a body organ you may have combined body systems, for example, musculoskeletal and neurological examination when examining the face. This is beneficial to the patient because they are spared from sitting up, lying down and again sitting up from time to time, which can be exhausting.</p>
<p>As covered earlier, the four fundamental processes which you will employ during physical examination of a patient, are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Inspection</li>
<li>Palpation</li>
<li>Percussion</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="auscultation">Auscultation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You have already gone through the process of physical examination in order to arrive at a nursing diagnosis. Now you will look at how to make a clinical diagnosis. Before performing a general physical examination, there are certain vital observations that you should take first, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Taking vital signs such as temperature, pulse, respirations and blood pressure, palpating, counting and describing the pulse</li>
<li>Measuring height, weight, fluid intake and output</li>
</ul>
<p>As you are performing the physical examination, you will also be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Auscultating for body sounds of the lungs, the abdomen and other organs. You will require a stethoscope</li>
<li>Palpating soft areas of the body to check for solid masses, abdominal rigidity or tenderness</li>
</ul>
<p>You can perform a physical examination anytime you are in a contact with the patient in any set-up, for example, while bathing a patient. Here you can obtain further information about the skin and the patient's response to activities. Move on to see how to perform a systematic examination, beginning with the skin</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-skin">The Skin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-skin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The examination of the skin includes observing the nails, skin colour, bruising/bleeding, lesions, oedema, moisture, temperature and elasticity. Inspect the nails for colour, shape and clubbing. Record the findings of any of the above areas.</p>
<p>The colour of the skin is an important indication of something wrong, either locally or systematically, when the colour is other than normal. Have a look at the significance of colour in the following table.</p>
<p>The Skin</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Colour</th><th>Terminology</th><th>Pathophysiology</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Redness</td><td>Inflammation</td><td>Is the result of the small blood vessels in the skin becoming dilated? This is seen in cases of fever, sunburn and local infection.</td></tr><tr><td>Blueness</td><td>Cyanosis</td><td>Is the result of lack of oxygen in the blood? Easily seen in the nail beds, lips and mucous membrane.</td></tr><tr><td>Yellow</td><td>Jaundice</td><td>Is due to increased bile pigments in blood.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Pale</th><th>Pallor</th><th>Is the result of a decrease in the number of red blood cells (anaemia)?</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Dark purple areas</td><td>Purpura</td><td>Large or small and are the result of ruptured blood vessels, either because of trauma or a systemic infection</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Skin lesions can be single or multiples. They can be small or large as well as different in colour, size, shape and skin layer involvement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="head">Head<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#head" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should palpate the cranium for any lumps, abrasions and asymmetry, while noting the condition of the hair.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neck">Neck<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neck" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Palpate the neck for asymmetry, distended veins, abnormal lymph nodes and enlargement of the thyroid. Then perform a range of motion of the neck to detect any limitations.</p>
<p>Place a stethoscope over the carotid artery to listen for any abnormal sound resulting from circulatory turbulence.</p>
<p>Palpation is a vital part of the physical examination. Many body structures even though not visible are accessible by hand and may be felt.</p>
<p>When examining the abdomen, auscultation is performed before palpation and percussion to avoid altering the bowel sounds.</p>
<p>Sounds generated within the body may be felt. For example, certain murmurs generated in the heart or within blood vessels (thrills) may be detected. Thrills cause sensation to the hand much like purring of a cat. Voice sounds are transmitted along the bronchi to the periphery of the lung. These may be perceived by touch and will be altered by certain disease states within the lungs.</p>
<p>This phenomenon is called tactile fremitus and is useful in assessing diseases of the chest. Now continue with your physical examination.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="eyes">Eyes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#eyes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You must test for visual acuity in the patient. One of the methods of screening a patient for visual activity is by asking them to read any available printed matter using one eye at a time.</p>
<p>Ask the patient to close one eye with a piece of paper, not with their hand.</p>
<p>This simple method will give you enough information to decide whether the patient has a visual acuity problem and the approximate degree of the problem.</p>
<p>Alternatively, visual acuity can be tested using a Schellen's chart. Visit any doctor's or clinical officer's clinic to familiarise yourself with this chart.</p>
<p>When undertaking the eye examination:</p>
<ul>
<li>Observe eyes for position and alignment to each other. Note the position of the eyelids in relationship to the eyeballs.</li>
<li>You will easily see oedema, discolouration, lesions and condition of the eyelids</li>
<li>Conjunctiva and sclera: You can easily check their condition by asking the patient to look up while you depress the lower lid</li>
<li>Also note the colour of the eye, presence of swelling nodules, cornea and lens. They should be clear. Watch out for any opacities. Discoloration of the conjunctiva and sclera could be due to jaundice, anaemia, or cyanosis</li>
<li>Pupils: observe the size, shape, and equality of the pupils using a flashlight or ophthalmoscope. Check that the pupils dilate and constrict equally when adjusting to dim or bright light</li>
<li>The optic disc is assessed for size and colour</li>
</ul>
<p>Move on now to review them together. Abnormalities may include swelling, discolouration, lesions, scaliness of the tissue around the eyes and so on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ears">Ears<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ears" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Inspect the outer ear for swelling, lesions and/or lumps with the head turned to the side. Then examine each ear with the otoscope for evidence of excess cerumen (wax) growth, redness or even discharge. You should then screen the patient by covering one ear. Standing two feet away from the patient towards the un-occluded ear softly whisper numbers, increasing the volume of your voice in stages. If the patient cannot hear, repeat the numbers you whispered. Test both ears the same way and note your findings.</p>
<p>Alternatively, you could test for hearing using a tuning fork, which you have to strike and hold at an equal distance from each ear to test for air conduction. Then you should place the vibrating tuning fork on each mastoid process, just below and behind the ears and then centre top of the cranium to test for bone conduction of sound.</p>
<p>Pull on ear to elicit tenderness. You then assess the eardrum (tympanic membrane) for signs of swelling, of colour change and for perforations. Look into the canal for discharge or wax.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 76 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nose">Nose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>With the patient's head slightly tilted back, inspect each nostril using a nasal spectrum. Inspect the cavities for colour, condition of the mucosa, bleeding and presence of foreign bodies or masses. Observe the size, shape, colour, and symmetry of the nose. Use a nasal spectrum to check the colour and continuity of mucosa.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-any-abnormalities-you-can-detect-during-a-physical-examination-of-the-nose">List any abnormalities you can detect during a physical examination of the nose.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-any-abnormalities-you-can-detect-during-a-physical-examination-of-the-nose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nose">Nose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>With the patient's head slightly tilted back, inspect each nostril using a nasal spectrum. Inspect the cavities for colour, condition of the mucosa, bleeding and presence of foreign bodies or masses. Observe the size, shape, colour, and symmetry of the nose. Use a nasal spectrum to check the colour and continuity of mucosa.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-any-abnormalities-you-can-detect-during-a-physical-examination-of-the-nose">List any abnormalities you can detect during a physical examination of the nose.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-any-abnormalities-you-can-detect-during-a-physical-examination-of-the-nose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>External structural deformity, asymmetry, inflammation, swelling, deflected nasal septum, bleeding, lesions, exudates and/or foreign bodies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mouth">Mouth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mouth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Examine the back of the throat using a flashlight and tongue blade (spatula). Look for swelling, redness, bacteria or viral patches, position and size of uvula. Check the nostrils by asking the patient to say, "Ah". Inspect the teeth for looseness and presence of caries. Observe the mucous of inner mouth for colour and presence of lesions. Ask the patient to clench the teeth and smile. This helps you to assess the bite and facial muscular tone. Note the colour and smoothness of the lips. Inspect lips for colour, lumps, ulcers or cracking, gums and teeth for inflammation, swelling, bleeding, retraction and discolouration of the gums.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharynx">Pharynx<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharynx" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Use a longer blade (spatula) to depress the arch of the tongue so that you can see the pharynx. Inspect the uvula, tonsils and posterior pharynx. Note the colour symmetry, evidence of exudates, oedema or ulceration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-chest">The Chest<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-chest" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You have already seen how to create rapport with the patient and how to make them comfortable. If you are examining a male patient remove the gown. For a female patient, untie the gown and part it for chest examination, so that the breast is exposed. Observe the level of shoulders for equality while the patient is sitting and facing you. Observe the pectoralis muscles on each side of the chest for symmetry as the patient presses the palms together and lifts the hands over the head.</p>
<p>Note any abnormal dimpling, colour or discharge of the nipples. You should ask a female patient to lie in the supine position, and examine each breast and palpate for masses or lumps from the nipple outward, then around the periphery and axilla.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inspection">Inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Observe the chest both from behind and from the front while the patient is sitting. Look for deformities of skeletal structures or bulges. Note any unequal movement during respiration.</p>
<p>Ask the patient to take a deep breath and look at the respiratory movements such as splinting. Watch for abnormalities of the skin such as rashes and lumps. Observe the rate and rhythm of breathing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="palpation-of-the-chest">Palpation of the Chest<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palpation-of-the-chest" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Palpation of the chest is aimed at identifying the size, shape and degree of resistance of various parts of vibrations. Identify areas of tenderness or pain, for example, deep or superficial. Evaluate areas observed with abnormality. Measure the expansion of the chest and locate the position of the trachea.</p>
<p>With the patient in supine position, palpate the neck veins for normal filling and percuss the cardiac margins (outline of the heart). Use a stethoscope to listen to the heart sounds. Replace the patient's gown.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="percussion">Percussion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#percussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Percussion is tapping the surface with a finger to produce a sound, which helps to determine the density of the underlying organs. This is done with the middle finger of your left hand as the pleximeter percusses over the distal interphalangeal of the right hand</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-e68fb346.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<p>The technique of percussion translates the application of physical force into sound. This is used to obtain information about diseases in the chest and abdomen.</p>
<p>The principle is to set the chest wall or abdominal wall into vibration by striking it with a firm object. The sound produced is reflective of the density of the underlying structure. Certain densities produce sounds that can be identified as percussion notes, for example:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tympani is a drum like sound produced by percussing the air filled stomach.</li>
<li>Resonance is a sound elicited over air filled lungs.</li>
<li>Hyper resonance is audible while percussing over inflated lung tissue of the patient with emphysema.</li>
<li>Dullness is the percussion of the liver that produces a dull sound.</li>
<li>Flatness is the percussion of the thigh that results in flatness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-percuss-the-chest">How to Percuss the Chest<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-percuss-the-chest" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Place the distal phalanx of the left middle finger firmly against the chest wall. The other fingers should be held away from the chest wall. This is because any pressure they might exert against the thorax would tend to mute or dampen the sound produced.</p>
<p>The right hand now becomes the striking object. The middle finger of the right hand is used to strike the terminal phalanx of the middle finger of the left hand just behind the nail bed. If done sharply, a brief resonant will be produced.</p>
<p>The motion of the right hand should be dominantly a wrist action. The fore-arm itself should be held steadily. The clarity of the sound produced is dependant on the brevity of the action. The intensity is the function of the force used.</p>
<p>Percussion gives one the capacity to assess the normal anatomical detail which involves:</p>
<ul>
<li>The degree to which the diaphragm descends during inspiration</li>
<li>Sounds over lung tissues are normally resonant</li>
<li>Sound over the diaphragm is dull</li>
</ul>
<p>You may determine the level of pleural effusion or location of pneumatic application consolidation or actelectasis of a lobe of the lung.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="auscultation">Auscultation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Auscultation is listening to the sounds, for example, of the lungs, heart, bowels, with a stethoscope. You can also use the same technique to listen to the foetal heart using a foetal-scope. Listening to the sounds helps in determining the airflow through the lungs and presence of fluid, mucous or obstruction in the air passages.</p>
<p>Abnormal sounds include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Rales, which are caused by moisture partially blocking air passage. The sounds produced by this blockage are not continuous and are heard mostly on inspiration. Rales are sign of pneumonia</li>
<li>Rhonchi, which are low-pitched continuous sounds, which originate in larger air passages</li>
<li>Wheezes, which are high-pitched hissing sounds originating in small air passageways</li>
<li>Crepitations, which are as a result of the fluid in the alveoli and are heard mostly in inspiration. Presence of fine crepitations is a sign of pneumonia or congestive heart failure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="auscultation">Auscultation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Auscultation is listening to the sounds, for example, of the lungs, heart, bowels, with a stethoscope. You can also use the same technique to listen to the foetal heart using a foetal-scope. Listening to the sounds helps in determining the airflow through the lungs and presence of fluid, mucous or obstruction in the air passages.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Abnormal sounds include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Rales, which are caused by moisture partially blocking air passage. The sounds produced by this blockage are not continuous and are heard mostly on inspiration. Rales are sign of pneumonia</li>
<li>Rhonchi, which are low-pitched continuous sounds, which originate in larger air passages</li>
<li>Wheezes, which are high-pitched hissing sounds originating in small air passageways</li>
<li>Crepitations, which are as a result of the fluid in the alveoli and are heard mostly in inspiration. Presence of fine crepitations is a sign of pneumonia or congestive heart failure</li>
</ul>
<p>Sound is produced within the body either by the movement of the air through hollow structures or by the forces set by the movement of columns of fluid that set solid structures in motion. The different sounds produced by various movements include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Movement of air through the trachea and bronchi (breath sounds)</li>
<li>Movement of air past function vocal cords (spoken voice)</li>
<li>Movement of air through the intestines (bowel sounds)</li>
<li>Movement of blood through vascular structures that provide critical resistance to the flow (murmurs)</li>
<li>The impedance to flowing blood provided by closed valves and the heart wall (heart sounds)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-3-clinical-diagnosis">SECTION 3: CLINICAL DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-clinical-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sound is produced within the body either by the movement of the air through hollow structures or by the forces set by the movement of columns of fluid that set solid structures in motion. The different sounds produced by various movements include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Movement of air through the trachea and bronchi (breath sounds)</li>
<li>Movement of air past function vocal cords (spoken voice)</li>
<li>Movement of air through the intestines (bowel sounds)</li>
<li>Movement of blood through vascular structures that provide critical resistance to the flow (murmurs)</li>
<li>The impedance to flowing blood provided by closed valves and the heart wall (heart sounds)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examination-of-the-cardiovascular-system">Examination of the Cardiovascular System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-the-cardiovascular-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="chest-and-heart">Chest and Heart<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chest-and-heart" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The following guidelines should be kept in mind when conducting a heart or chest examination. Inspect the anterior chest for bulges and pulsation. Palpate the anterior chest for localised areas of tenderness. Identify the point of maximum impulse, known as the "apex beat". The apex beat (PMI) is a point of maximum impulse. PMI is the lowermost and the outermost point at which the heart beat can be felt maximally.</p>
<p>The apex beat is a vibration of the chest wall that is caused by an impulse transferred from the apex of the heart. The location of the apex beat is directly over the apex, approximately 7 to 9 cm (3 to 3 Â½ inches) from the mid-sternal line at the fifth inter-costal space.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="auscultation">Auscultation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are two heart sounds, which make up one combined sound, best described as "lubdub". Listen for any other sounds apart from the heart sounds. The areas of auscultation are:</p>
<ul>
<li>M-Mitral = 5th inter-costal space</li>
<li>P-Pulmonary = 2nd inter-costal space</li>
<li>A-Aortic = 2nd inter-costal space</li>
<li>T-Triscupid = 5th inter-costal space</li>
</ul>
<p>Abnormalities, which you may detect during auscultation include:</p>
<ul>
<li>An enlarged heart or something in the chest displacing the mediastinum can cause shifting apex beat. An enlarged heart may be secondary to hypertension or vascular heart disease</li>
<li>Irregular heart sounds seen in ischaemic heart disease and thyrotoxicosis</li>
<li>Heart murmurs found in rheumatic heart disease, congenital heart disease and occasionally in severe anaemia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="peripheral-pulses">Peripheral Pulses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#peripheral-pulses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The first step in checking for peripheral pulses is to palpate the right radial pulse. Record the rhythm, rate, volume and character. Compare the right radial with the left radial. Note the rate and rhythm. Palpate the right femoral pulse and then compare the right femoral to the right. Palpate the right popliteal and compare it to</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>the left. Note the temperature of the legs and observe any dilated veins in the legs. Palpate for the presence of pitting oedema in the leg and over the sacrum. To examine the neck for distended veins, place the patient in the semi recumbent position (45 degrees).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-3ecd1756.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-45cbace1.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examining-the-lymphatic-and-musculoskeletal-system">Examining the Lymphatic and Musculoskeletal System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examining-the-lymphatic-and-musculoskeletal-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="lymphatic-system">Lymphatic system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lymphatic-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>While you are assessing the patient's musculoskeletal and peripheral vascular function, you should also palpate for the lymph nodes at their normal location, for example:</p>
<ul>
<li>Neck, that is, sub mental, submandibular, occipital, cervical</li>
<li>Axillary, that is, central, pectoral, lateral</li>
<li>Inguinal</li>
</ul>
<p>Swollen lymph nodes may exhibit several characteristics, including, tenderness, fluctuation, firmness and hardness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="musculoskeletal-system">Musculoskeletal system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#musculoskeletal-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The musculoskeletal system can be evaluated at the same time as the peripheral/ vascular and lymphatic systems.</p>
<p>This system comprises bones, which support the body, muscles that move the bones by pulling on them and joints, which allow movement. Bones do not touch. Cartilage covers the joint ends of all bones and offers a cushion between the bony surfaces. There is also a space between bones covered with fluid, which serves as a lubricant.</p>
<p>The joint structure regulates the amount of movement possible, for example, the joint between the humerus and scapula (shoulder joint) has a greater range of motion than the joint between the radius/ulna and humerus (elbow joint).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-abnormalities-might-you-find-in-the-system">What abnormalities might you find in the system?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-abnormalities-might-you-find-in-the-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There could be deviation from the normal range of motion such as limitation, stiffness or instability. You may observe joint swelling or deformity; warmth; redness or decreased</p>
<p>strength. Next you should test for power of the arm, grip, fingers, wrist, leg, foot and thigh.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examination-of-the-breast">Examination of the Breast<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-the-breast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a very important examination. You will find that you will perform it in general nursing as well as in reproductive health, that is, in midwifery and family planning. You will need to reflect on your knowledge of the anatomy and physiology of the female reproductive organs.</p>
<p>Conducting a female breast examination is a diagnostic aid in the early detection of lumps, growths or thickening in the breast. Ask the patient to undress but cover the breast until the examination begins to maintain privacy. Place a flat pillow or a folded towel under the patient's shoulders.</p>
<p>As you conduct the examination, teach the patient how to examine her breasts monthly after the menstrual period or at regular monthly intervals and after menopause.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-do-you-perform-breast-examination">How do you perform breast examination?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-do-you-perform-breast-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ask the patient/client to sit, arms at her side, facing you. Inspect the breast for size and equality, shape and colour. Note whether there is any puckering or dimpling of the skin or deviation of the nipples. Repeat the inspection with the patient's arms raised over the head. Recline the patient on a flat bed or examination couch and place a folded towel under the shoulders on the same side as the breast to be examined. Position the patient's relaxed arm on that side so as to allow it to rest comfortably over her head. Now think of the breast as a wheel or clock. Begin the examination at the top of the breast, or 12.00 o'clock, with the flat of the fingers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inspection">Inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Inspect the breasts for size and symmetry, contour, appearance of the skin; observe nipple size and shape, rashes or ulcers discharge and retraction.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-47050138.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="palpation">Palpation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palpation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Palpate the breast, moving from the outer portion of the breast towards the nipple and using light circular movements until the entire breast is covered in this manner. Then feel the area over the nipple carefully with the flat of fingers. With the arm down at the patient's side, examine the tissues of the breasts, which extend into the armpit or axillary region, feeling for lymph nodes in this area.</p>
<p>Palpate the breast, compressing the breast tissue between your finger and chest wall in a systematic manner and noting the position of any unexplained tissue masses. Palpate the nipples noting elasticity, discharge. Repeat the process for the other breast. Abnormalities that may be noted include lumps, nodules, masses, discharge from the nipples and colour of the skin.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-c0533c4a.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-312046c5.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg">
Woman lies on pillow with right arm raised left hand palpates right breast with pads of fingers.
Woman lies on pillow with left arm raised above head, fingers of right hand squeeze nipple of left breast.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="remember-teach-the-patient-to-perform-breast-examination-correctly-at-home-at-regular-monthly-intervals">Remember: teach the patient to perform breast examination correctly at home, at regular monthly intervals.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember-teach-the-patient-to-perform-breast-examination-correctly-at-home-at-regular-monthly-intervals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examination-of-the-abdomen">Examination of the Abdomen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-the-abdomen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Before performing the examination, ask the patient to empty their bladder.</p>
<p>Put the patient in supine position and make them comfortable. Inspect the whole abdomen for contours, distension and asymmetry.</p>
<p>Ask the patient to point to any area of pain but examine that area last.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inspection">Inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should begin with an inspection of the skin. Look for scars, stretch marks, dilated veins, rashes and lesions. Note their colour, size and shape. Study the contours of the skin, noting any distortions in shape, localised budges and masses. Finally, note the condition of the umbilicus.</p>
<p>Palpation of the abdomen will allow you to identify the position of abdominal organs and masses. Using the pads of your fingers, feel in all four quadrants (superficial and deep). Palpate for liver, spleen, kidneys and the bladder. With the patient breathing deeply with knees flexed, palpate the abdomen for organs and masses on expiration. Using your fingers, you can feel for the position of abdominal structures. Grasp the skin between the fingers to test for dehydration.</p>
<p>Perform percussion to test shifting dullness, which indicates the presence of fluid (ascites).</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-1520844f.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="auscultation">Auscultation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Listen to all the four quadrants noting the frequency and the type of bowel sounds. Use a stethoscope to listen to the bowel sounds. You may be able to detect the following abnormalities in the abdomen:</p>
<ul>
<li>Masses - note the location, size, shape, consistency, tenderness, pulsation and mobility.</li>
<li>Enlargement - as you palpate the liver, kidney and spleen note for pain and irregularity.</li>
<li>Bowel sounds - they are absent in cases of paralytic ileus in peritonitis or hyperactive in intestinal obstruction.</li>
</ul>
<p>In a thin patient you may palpate the liver edge, portions of the large bowel, the pulsating aorta and iliac arteries and the lower pole of the right kidney</p>
<p>Examination of the Genitalia, Anus and Rectum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="male-genitalia">Male Genitalia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-genitalia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Examine male patients in the standing position so that the inguinal ring can be palpated for herniation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="penis">Penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Observe the skin, prepuce of foreskin, if present, the glans and the urethral meatus. Note and record any lesions, scars and drainage nodules. If the patient is uncircumcised, retract the foreskin of the penis and inspect for irritation, ulceration and presence of lesions.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-c37a9918.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="scrotum">Scrotum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scrotum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Observe the skin for nodules and lesions, swelling. Palpate testicles, noting the size, shape, tenderness and consistency. Palpate the epididymis and spermatic cord. Once again, note size, tenderness and consistency.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prostate">Prostate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prostate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This will be discussed with rectal examination. Observe the hernias while a patient is standing. Ask the patient to cough and try to reduce the masses if possible. The abnormalities you should keep an eye out for include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Syphilitic changes, that is, circular, dark red painless ulcer</li>
<li>Urethral discharge thick pus drainage which indicates gonorrhoea</li>
<li>Hydrocele, that is, a non-tender fluid filled mass confined to the scrotum</li>
<li>Hernias, which may be arising outside the scrotum</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="female-genitalia">Female Genitalia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#female-genitalia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You should examine a female patient in the lithotomy position (that is heels together, knees apart) with knees flexed. Drape the patient using a clean sheet or bath blanket as you would for catheterisation. The patient should be on an examination couch with stirrups where possible. Have a gooseneck lamp, put on sterile gloves and lubricate the outside of vaginal speculum (the inside is not lubricated because the presence of jelly interferes with the accuracy of the papanicolau (papa test).</p>
<p>The test is done by obtaining secretions from the cervical os on a swab. The secretions are examined for the presence of abnormal cells.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>After inspecting the cervix, remove the speculum.</p>
<p>Then lubricate the index finger and middle finger of one hand. Insert the fingers into the vagina, pushing downward on the patient's abdomen just above the symphsisis pubis with the other hand. Palpate the uterus and ovaries. Assess the organs for location, size, outline, masses and tenderness. This examination is usually done along with pelvic examination.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-a58b0a30.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<p>Observe the external genitalia for inflammation, ulceration, discharge, swelling or nodules. Palpate any lesions and note tenderness. Pelvic examination and bimanual palpation then follow. You should comment on the size of the uterus, any tenderness, and any ovarian mass.</p>
<p>Try to name at least five abnormalities that you might detect</p>
<p>Some abnormalities you might detect include hypertrophy of the clitoris; imperforate hymen; Bartholin's cyst or abscess; vaginal discharge; fibroids; uterine prolapse or signs of cancer.</p>
<p>Anus and Rectum</p>
<p>Rectal examination is usually performed after genital examination and after pelvis examination.</p>
<p>The patient can be examined in two positions. The patient can either bend over the side of the bed or assume the lithotomy position, with the penis and testes held aside, or the knee chest position.</p>
<p>Put on gloves, lubricate the gloved fingers then insert the middle finger and palpate for size of the lower masses, internal haemorrhoids and tenderness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-examinations">Other Examinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-examinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="examination-of-arms-hands-and-fingers">Examination of Arms, Hands and Fingers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-arms-hands-and-fingers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>With the patient seated or standing, ask them to extend both arms out in front of the body.</p>
<ul>
<li>Examine the musculature for asymmetry and palpate for turgor</li>
<li>Range the arms, hand and fingers to assess agility</li>
<li>Observe the skin for lesions, spotting and general colour</li>
<li>Palpate the joints and observe for nodules and enlargement</li>
<li>Observe the hands for colour and feel the temperature</li>
<li>Observe the hands for any deviations of the alignment of fingers</li>
<li>Observe the nails for hardness and general condition</li>
<li>Test for the grip of each hand</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="examination-of-the-back">Examination of the Back<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-the-back" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Place the patient in the prone position or let them sit in the bed with the back facing you. Expose the back and examine the skin for spots and lesions. Note the curvature of the spine and palpate the vertebral column.</p>
<p>When examining school age children, check for scholiosis (lateral curvature of the spine) by looking for asymmetry of shoulder and hips while observing the child from behind. Observe for asymmetry or prominence of the rib cage while watching the child bend over so that the back is parallel to the floor. Listen to the lower lobes of the lungs with the stethoscope.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="examination-of-the-nervous-system">Examination of the Nervous System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examination-of-the-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The nervous system is an extremely complex network, which acts to coordinate the functions of the body. It includes the brain, spinal cord and peripheral nerves. You will review the details in unit three of module one. When examining the nervous system, you should integrate it into other aspects of the physical examination, which will now be addressed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="mental-status">Mental Status<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-status" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Observe the patient's general level of consciousness, ask "who" and "where" they are and observe for slurring of speech.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="motor-function">Motor Function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#motor-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Note the gait and balance. Palpate each leg for muscle bulk and observe for discolouration, temperature and skin condition. Dorsiflex each foot to check for calf pain, a possible sign of thrombophlebitis (Herman's signs). Take pedal pulses on each foot and compare them. Palpate the ankles with fingers to assess for pitting oedema. Test strength by having the</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>patient press the sole of the feet against your palm. Extend and flex arms at elbow and the feet at ankle while you apply pressure. Inspect joints for enlargement. Observe muscles of arms and legs for size and uniformity</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kerning-s-signs">Kerning's Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kerning-s-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is another test for meningitis. Lay the patient on their back. Flex the hip to 90 degrees (straight up) allowing the knee to flex. Then extend the knee. If the meningeal inflammation is present there will be pain and irritation and sometimes a tendency to flex the neck.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sensation">Sensation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Check light touch and pin prick sensation. Have the patient indicate (with eyes closed) when they feel the touch of cotton wool and then of a pin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meningeal-signs">Meningeal Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningeal-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Looking for shifting of the neck with the patient lying down most easily tests meningeal inflammation. Bend the head towards the chest. If neck shifting is present there will be pain and resistance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="testing-reflexes">Testing Reflexes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#testing-reflexes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are many muscle reflexes, which you can test. The most important ones are those of the biceps and the triceps in the arms and knee (patellar) and ankle (Achilles) in the leg. The response is obtained by striking the tendon with the muscle relaxed or slightly tensed. Reflexes are graded as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>0 absent (no response)</li>
<li>1+ reduced (hypoactive)</li>
<li>2 + normal</li>
<li>3 + increased (hyperactive)</li>
<li>4 + markedly increased with clonus (continued contraction of the muscle)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="corneal-reflex">Corneal Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corneal-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Corneal reflex (blink) is tested by touching the cornea with a soft, small wet cotton, the patient should blink.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biceps-reflex">Biceps Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biceps-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Biceps Reflex is tested as follows. Place your thumb on the biceps tendon, which is located just above the antecubital fosse. Striking the thumb should cause flexion of the forearm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="triceps-reflex">Triceps Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#triceps-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To test the triceps reflex, the upper arm is supported at a right angle to the body and the forearm is allowed to hang freely. The triceps tendons is then struck with the reflex hammer just above the elbow. Extension of the forearm should occur.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="branchioradio">Branchioradio<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#branchioradio" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The branchioradio reflex is tested by striking the radius slightly above the wrist with the reflex hammer. This should cause flexion and supination of the forearm.</p>
