<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="knee-reflex">Knee Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#knee-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To test for knee reflex, the patient's lower leg must be relaxed and hanging freely from the knee. When you strike the patellar tendon, which is just below the knee with the reflex hammer, extension of the leg should occur.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ankle-reflex">Ankle Reflex<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ankle-reflex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When testing for ankle reflex, hold the foot of the patient in a position of dorsiflexion, then strike the Achille's tendon at the back of the ankle with the reflex hammer. This should cause plaster reflexion of the foot, that is, the toes should bend downwards.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-abnormalities-are-you-likely-to-detect">What abnormalities are you likely to detect?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-abnormalities-are-you-likely-to-detect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are abnormalities you may detect:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mental status: decreased level of consciousness, confusion, hyperactivity</li>
<li>Motor function: weakness, atrophy and cord lesion, lack of balance, and lack of coordination, cord or brain lesion</li>
<li>Sensation: decreased or loss of sense of touch, cord lesion</li>
<li>Meningeal signs: presence of signs of meningeal irritation</li>
<li>Reflexes: increased or decreased reflex response</li>
</ul>
<p>You have gone through a comprehensive head to toe physical examination and have seen the abnormalities that may be detected. Now you will briefly see how you can arrive at a clinical diagnosis.</p>
<p>You started with history taking such as personal/social, medical, past and present. You also looked at the presenting complaints and found that there will be a chief or major presenting complaint and, possibly, accompanying complaints or signs and symptoms.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Signs and Symptoms Flowchart</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-1c142581.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<p>The flowchart also provides other examples of specific signs and symptoms that may lead to a clinical diagnosis.</p>
<p>To arrive at a clinical diagnosis you have to match major complaints and examination/investigation results.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example">Example:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Presenting complaint: A cough, which is productive.</li>
<li>Accompanying symptom: Dyspnoea, on examination rhonchi detected.</li>
<li>Diagnosis: Pneumonia.</li>
<li>Symptoms: Cough, which is productive for more than four weeks, sweating at night with weight loss.</li>
<li>Sputum for AFB: Positive.</li>
<li>Chest X-ray: Shows opacity.</li>
<li>Clinical Diagnosis: Pulmonary tuberculosis.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="integrated-management-of-adolescent-and-adult-illness-imai">Integrated Management of Adolescent and Adult Illness [IMAI]<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#integrated-management-of-adolescent-and-adult-illness-imai" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>IMAI is a health care strategy that addresses the overall health care of the patient. It focuses on the main clinical conditions that account for most of the deaths among adolescents and adults. It integrates the prevention of illnesses and care into a single health care package. If you use this approach, you will find it more rewarding and it will make your work easier.</p>
<p>Move on to take a look at the rationale for using IMAI.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rationale-and-benefits-of-imai">Rationale and Benefits of IMAI<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rationale-and-benefits-of-imai" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Each year many adults and adolescents die prematurely of simple and preventable illnesses. When people seek treatment, they may get treated for single illnesses. However, health workers are reflecting upon a more integrated approach. This is because in many cases it may not be easy to make a single diagnosis with the limited resources. In any case, when patients present to you, they may have multiple complaints that do not point to just one diagnosis.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>IMAI extends the benefits of Integrated Management of Diseases to Adolescents and Adults who are a neglected group. Furthermore, the strategy combines preventive strategies even for the management of chronic illnesses.</p>
<p>There are several benefits to the use of an integrated management approach for adolescent and adult illnesses. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>It addresses the major adolescent and adult problems</li>
<li>It responds to demand</li>
<li>It also focuses on chronic diseases and their treatment, for example, HIV/AIDS</li>
<li>It balances prevention and care</li>
<li>It addresses special needs of the special groups</li>
<li>It invests care in the community</li>
<li>It promotes cost savings</li>
<li>It improves equity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="imai-interventions">IMAI interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#imai-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The IMAI has simplified guidelines, which give several possible combinations of a large number of interventions. The interventions are based on key clinical symptoms.</p>
<p>Every country must develop and adopt core interventions that are related to prevalent diseases in their communities.</p>
<p>The interventions are centred on: acute care; chronic care; HIV care; palliative care; tuberculosis and emergency treatment. When our country finally adopts and develops these guidelines, they will be very useful.</p>
<p>This approach to care is based on the experience with IMCI. The preventive interventions within IMAI include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Provision of key information on HIV</li>
<li>Voluntary HIV testing and counselling</li>
<li>Counselling on sexually transmitted infections, for example, syphilis</li>
<li>Counselling on safer sex</li>
<li>Sharing health messages on harmful alcohol use, smoking, inactivity, poor diet and so on</li>
<li>Special adolescent preventive interventions, for example, insecticide treated nets, tetanus vaccinations and blood screening</li>
<li>Adult's preventive intervention</li>
<li>Interventions to prevent mother to child transmission of HIV, through family planning and early antenatal care</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-4-principles-of-safe-drug-use">SECTION 4: PRINCIPLES OF SAFE DRUG USE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-4-principles-of-safe-drug-use" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In section three you studied how to diagnose and treat minor illnesses.</p>
<p>In this section, we will cover the principles of the Essential Drugs Kit, therapeutic doses and calculations of drugs in common use, drug interaction, drug assimilation, drug resistance, contraindications and side effects.</p>
<p>This section aims at building on the knowledge you already have on safe drug use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the therapeutic doses and calculation of drugs in common use</li>
<li>Describe drug interaction, drug assimilation, drug resistance, contraindications and side effects</li>
<li>Describe the principles of essential drugs kit</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="pharmacology">Pharmacology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You were taught pharmacology for nurses during your KECHN training. Since then you have been administering drugs to patients.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-definition-of-pharmacology">The Definition of Pharmacology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-definition-of-pharmacology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You may have come up with various definitions. Admittedly, there are many definitions of pharmacology. The most widely accepted one states, 'Pharmacology is the science of drugs, which includes their preparation, use and effects'.</p>
<p>In this definition the core word is 'drugs'. Most people, when defining drugs, think of only medicinal drugs that are prescribed by a doctor to treat illness. What about substances like caffeine, alcohol, nicotine and tobacco? What about the illegal drugs that are often abused or the environmental substances that have physiological effects when they come into contact with the body?</p>
<p>In view of this, the broader definition of pharmacology is 'the study of the effects of chemical substances on living tissues'. You are aware that every culture has studied plants and has developed a system of medicine founded on the use of plants. The common term used for this kind of treatment is herbal medicine. The government is in the process of regulating what is commonly known as alternative medicine.</p>
<p>You must be asking yourself a few questions about the significance of pharmacology in</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>nursing. You have a responsibility in the administration of drugs. You are expected to exercise judgment in the management of drug therapy. You require an understanding of drug action and the ability to detect both therapeutic and adverse reactions in the patient. You are also expected to counsel patients on the management of their drug regimens for optimal effect.</p>
<p>In your nursing practice at times you diagnose and treat minor illnesses and are involved in the prescribing of medications.</p>
<p>As a registered community health nurse you will be expected to promote health and prevent drug related diseases. You will, therefore, be concerned with the health impact of environment pollutants and health aspects of social, medicinal and illegal drug use. You will be teaching the community on how to avoid drug hazards and prevent chemically induced disease.</p>
<p>Whether practising community health nursing or occupational health nursing, you will be involved in the early detection of drug related problems through case finding and referral. In addition, you will work with patients to improve self-care practices in home-based care. When administering drugs you must detect early signs and symptoms of toxicity, adverse reactions and drug interactions as well as therapeutic responses.</p>
<p>You have now seen why it is important for you to learn pharmacology. Your overall role is to promote responsible use of chemicals to enhance health, at the same time minimising the detrimental effects of such use. You are, therefore, required to utilise your knowledge of the human anatomy and physiology, legal aspects of nursing, that is, ethics and law pertaining to nursing practice. Remember that you covered the laws relating to nursing practice in unit one.</p>
<p>When administering drug therapy, you must be skilled in practical technical procedures required to handle, control and administer drugs safely.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laws-relating-to-the-control-of-drugs">Laws Relating to the Control of Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laws-relating-to-the-control-of-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You may be asking yourself whether it is necessary for you to have a wide knowledge of the legislation governing the administration and supply of drugs and to some extent you do. As a nurse of the twenty first century, you must have this knowledge because of the expanding roles of the nurse, especially the community health nurse.</p>
<p>As discussed earlier, an understanding of pharmacology and the reasons for storing drugs, in particular is essential. This knowledge will enable you to have confidence so as to ensure your safety and the safety of the patient when dealing with substances, which could be harmful. The regulations governing the administration of drugs may be divided into two: those that are statutory, relating to various Acts of Parliament and those that are institutional policies.</p>
<p>The aim of this legislation is proper management of drugs so as to prevent error, illegal usage and addiction. The persons chiefly affected by the statutes are doctors, pharmacists, nurses and clinical officers.</p>
<p>In Kenya, just like any other country in the world, there are elaborate legislative controls governing drug use. These laws restrict the production, distribution, prescription and administration of drugs.</p>
<p>You must:</p>
<ul>
<li>Be familiar with the regulations affecting drug use in your area of practice</li>
<li>Continually update yourself on the changes in drug regulations</li>
<li>Know the policies of the institution you are working in.</li>
<li>Abide by the drug control laws within your professional practice</li>
</ul>
<p>As you are advising patients on the use of drugs, you must not recommend the use of illegal substances or provide drugs for patients' use without proper prescription. You must maintain the security of drugs at all times to prevent diversion to unauthorised persons. For example, medication should be stored in locked cupboards. Some drugs must be kept under double locks. During drug administration all unlocked drugs must be kept under direct observation and control. Maintain careful records of the disposition of each dose of certain drugs such as DDA (narcotic drugs and psychotropic substances).</p>
<p>The patient has the final control on drug use. Normally, the patient gives or withholds consent to treatment and also determines compliance. You are, therefore, to ascertain the patient's drug attitudes and practices during the assessment. Explain carefully the need to change old habits. Give clear explanations and descriptions of drug regimens. You must respect the client's refusal for treatment and drug therapy.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 86 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 87 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-pharmacy-and-poisons-act-chapter-244-of-the-laws-of-kenya-1989">The Pharmacy and Poisons Act: Chapter 244 of the Laws of Kenya, 1989<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-pharmacy-and-poisons-act-chapter-244-of-the-laws-of-kenya-1989" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The Pharmacy and Poisons Act: Chapter 244 of the Laws of Kenya, 1989</p>
<p>This law requires the registration of all sellers of poisons. The act deals with the registration of pharmacists, defining statutory poisons, and drawing up the poisons list, which is divided into two parts:</p>
<p>Part I: Consists of those poisons which are not to be sold except by authorised sellers of poisons and by licensed wholesale dealers and dealers in mining, agricultural or horticultural accessories;</p>
<p>Part II: Consists of those poisons which are not to be sold except by persons entitled to sell Part I poisons and by persons licensed under section 32.</p>
<p>The Poisons Act, 1989 sets out various schedules which deal with the sale, labelling and colour of certain poisons. The schedules relevant to nursing are Schedule 1(5.1) and Schedule 4(5.4).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schedule-1-5-1">Schedule 1(5.1)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schedule-1-5-1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Poisons contained in the first schedule must be stored in a locked cupboard and must be adequately labelled. In hospital, they may be supplied only on a prescription signed by a registered medical practitioners or on a written order from the nurse in charge of the ward or the deputy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schedule-4-5-4">Schedule 4 (5.4)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schedule-4-5-4" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Poisons contained in the fourth schedule are divided into two parts.</p>
<ol>
<li>S.4 A. This group is used in medicine and must be ordered on a prescription by a registered doctor or dentist and bears the:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Name and address of doctor and patient</li>
<li>Name of the drug</li>
<li>Quantity to be supplied</li>
<li>Dose to be taken and if the prescription may be repeated</li>
<li>Signature of the doctor and the date</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>S.4 B. These drugs must be ordered on prescription but it requires only the date and doctor's signature. All schedule 4.A poisons are automatically included in the first schedule and are, therefore, kept in a locked cupboard. The pharmacist is required to keep schedule 4.A. prescriptions for two years.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-narcotic-drugs-and-psychotropic-substances-control-act-1994">The Narcotic Drugs and Psychotropic Substances (Control) Act, 1994<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-narcotic-drugs-and-psychotropic-substances-control-act-1994" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is an Act of Parliament to make provision with respect to the control of the possession of, and trafficking in, narcotic drugs and psychotropic substances and cultivation of certain plants, to provide for forfeiture of property derived from, or used in, illicit traffic narcotic drugs and psychotropic substances and for connected purposes.</p>
<p>The Act sets up an Advisory Council to review any drugs likely to be misused and determine if it could constitute a social problem. The Advisory Council also advises the minister on particular measures to be taken to prevent misuse of drugs or to deal with problems created by their use by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Restricting the availability of such drugs</li>
<li>Providing facilities for the rehabilitation of dependant persons</li>
<li>Educating the public in the dangers of misusing drugs</li>
<li>Promoting research into these drug problems</li>
</ul>
<p>The Act gives power to the minister to prevent the misuse of controlled drugs including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Searching premises</li>
<li>Obtaining information from doctors and pharmacists</li>
<li>Power to arrest</li>
<li>Prosecution and punishment of offenders</li>
</ul>
<p>The Act gives schedules of controlled drugs, which are regulated by the Act as:</p>
<ul>
<li>First schedule which is a list of narcotic drugs.</li>
<li>Second schedule which is a list of psychotropic substances</li>
<li>Third schedule, which is a list of prohibited plants, including cannabis, coca bush and paupers</li>
<li>some of the other drugs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prescribing-controlled-drugs">Prescribing Controlled Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prescribing-controlled-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The medical practitioner must write the prescription in ink and in their own handwriting giving the following details:</p>
<ul>
<li>Date</li>
<li>Name and address of the patient</li>
<li>Address of the doctor</li>
<li>Dose to be taken</li>
<li>Preparation</li>
<li>The form (mixture, tablets, ointments and so on)</li>
<li>The strength (in words and figures e.g. ten milligrams, 10 mg)</li>
<li>The quantity (in words and figures e.g. thirty millilitres, 30 mls or total number in</li>
</ul>
<p>words and figures, e.g. twenty tablets, 20 tabs)</p>
<p>In hospital the use of the patient's prescription sheet or case notes is adequate and the address of the patient or doctor is not required.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-supply-of-controlled-drugs">The Supply of Controlled Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-supply-of-controlled-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The pharmacist may only supply the drugs if:</p>
<ul>
<li>The medical practitioner lives in the country</li>
<li>The signature is known to them and believed to be genuine</li>
<li>The containers are that for controlled drugs which must state the kind of preparation (tablets, capsules, and ampoules), the strength of each unit dose and the total number of unit doses</li>
<li>In the case of mixtures, ointments, cream containers must state the total amount prepared and the percentage of each controlled drug they contain</li>
</ul>
<p>Within hospitals certain rules must be observed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hospital-rules">Hospital Rules<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hospital-rules" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Within hospitals certain rules must be observed.</p>
<ul>
<li>Prescriptions must be signed by a registered medical practitioner</li>
<li>Stock must be ordered from the dispensary in special controlled drug books signed by the nursing officer in charge/charge nurse or the deputy</li>
<li>Drugs must be delivered in a sealed container and a receipt signed by the ward in charge</li>
<li>Controlled drugs must be stored in a locked container or cupboard within a locked cupboard</li>
<li>These cupboards should not be used for any other purposes (for example, storing valuables)</li>
<li>Details of doses given to each patient must be recorded in cardex, together with the signature of the nurse giving the dose and the person checking it</li>
<li>Any drug wasted must be recorded and signed for</li>
<li>Controlled drug books must be kept for two years following the last entry date</li>
<li>All dangerous drugs are automatically contained in Schedule 1</li>
</ul>
<p>A practising midwife may administer on her own responsibility an injection of Pethidine, Buscopan or Egormetrine.</p>
<p>When prescribing controlled drugs the medical practitioner must write the prescription in ink and in their own handwriting. Think of all the details that must be included on the prescription?</p>
<ul>
<li>The date</li>
<li>Name and address of the patient</li>
<li>Address of the doctor</li>
<li>Dose to be taken</li>
<li>Preparation</li>
<li>The form (mixture, tablets, ointments and so on)</li>
<li>The strength (in words and figures e.g. ten milligrams and 10mg)</li>
<li>The quantity (in words and figures e.g. thirty millilitres and 30 mls or total number in words and figures e.g. twenty tablets and 20 tabs)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="local-regulations">Local Regulations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#local-regulations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Local regulations are devised by individual hospitals and are meant to protect their staff, particularly the nurse during training:</p>
<ul>
<li>Any dangerous drugs should be checked by a registered/enrolled nurse</li>
<li>Only a small quantity should be kept in the ward</li>
<li>The stock should be checked regularly</li>
<li>The drug keys should be on the person who is in charge of the word or the deputy</li>
<li>Ampoules containing different drugs should be stored separately</li>
<li>Drugs should not be transferred from one bottle to another</li>
<li>Out of date drugs and those brought in by patients should be returned immediately to the dispensary</li>
<li>Drug bottles must be labelled by a pharmacist</li>
</ul>
<p>What are you advised to do before administering any drugs when you go to work in a new hospital?</p>
<p>Any nurse entering a new hospital is advised to enquire about the hospital policies regarding drug administration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-standards">Drug Standards<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-standards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You looked into standards of nursing practice in unit one while discussing professional practice.</p>
<p>In your opinion, what are drug standards?</p>
<p>Standards are the yardsticks by which drug preparations are judged. As you have seen earlier, the standards for drug quality are established and enforced by the government. Medicines vary in their purity, strength, bioavailability, efficacy and safety or toxicity.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 88 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Standards of these or other properties must provide a method for measuring the attribute to be evaluated as well as an acceptable level or range for those measurements.</p>
<p>Take a look at these Drug Standards one by one.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="purity">Purity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A pure drug contains only a specific chemical agent with no contaminating ingredients. Drugs are not 100% pure because of the impurities from raw materials used for manufacturing them. Other ingredients are added to the chemical to manipulate the absorption process. These additives include solvents, fillers, disintegrators, buffers, waxes, dyes, inks and plastics.</p>
<p>Contaminants from the environment of the production plant may find their way into a batch of drugs. Standards of purity, therefore, rarely require that the substance in question be 100% drug chemical. They do, however, specify the type and concentration of extraneous substances allowed to be present in the drug product.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="potency">Potency<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The potency or the strength of a drug is measured by assay techniques.</p>
<p>Chemical analysis is used to determine the ingredients present in a preparation and their relative amounts</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bioavailability">Bioavailability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bioavailability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Bioavailability is the degree to which a drug can be absorbed and transported by the body to its site of action. This may be influenced by particle size, crystalline structure, solubility and polarity of the drug compound.</p>
<p>Bioavailability is commonly measured by blood or tissue concentration of the drug at a specified time following administration of a dose.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="efficacy">Efficacy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#efficacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Efficacy is the effectiveness of a drug in treatment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safety-or-toxicity">Safety or Toxicity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safety-or-toxicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Safety or toxicity is measured by the incidence and severity of reported adverse reactions following the use of a drug.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-do-you-interpret-drug-data">How do you interpret drug data?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-do-you-interpret-drug-data" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To be able to interpret drug data intelligently, you must:</p>
<ul>
<li>Be familiar with the signature of each property and the limitations of the testing procedures used to measure it</li>
<li>Evaluate therapeutic responses in patients receiving medication</li>
<li>Monitor adverse or toxic effects because if adverse reactions are diagnosed earlier it becomes easier to treat them</li>
</ul>
<p>Should you be involved in clinical trials of experimental drugs on human subjects, you will need to assess the patients appropriately so as to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Protect patients from serious harm stemming from their exposure to unproven drugs</li>
<li>Generate valid data for evaluation of the experimental drugs</li>
</ul>
<p>You must have observed that from time to time various new drugs are introduced into the market. Move on to look at various concepts that relate to safe drug use.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="name-of-drug">Name of Drug<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#name-of-drug" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A drug may be prescribed using various names, such as the trade name, generic name, and/or chemical name. You should be aware of the various names of drugs. You should also be aware of the different drug families.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-name">Chemical Name<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-name" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The chemical name of a drug indicates its atomic and molecular structure. These names are commonly used by the chemist and/or the research pharmacist. The names are unsuitable for general use since they are long.</p>
<p>Examples of chemical names include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Acetylsalicylic acid (C6H4OHCOOC1H5)</li>
<li>7-Chloro-10 (3-dimethlyamino-n-propy)</li>
<li>phenothiazine hydrochloride</li>
<li>4-hydroxyacetanilide-p-acetami dopherol</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260110-f9a35c12.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="generic-name">Generic Name<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generic-name" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A generic name (some call it approved name) is a simpler, shorter name for each drug substance. The name is often proposed by the company that first develops the drug. Examples of generic names include:</p>
<ul>
<li>acetylsalicylic acid commonly known as aspirin</li>
<li>7 chloro-z methyl-amino-sphenyl-3h-1, benco diazepine, 4oxide commonly known as chlordiazepoxide</li>
<li>2-chloro-10(3-dimiethylamino-n-n-propyl) pherothiazine hydrochloride commonly known as chlorpromazine</li>
<li>4 hydroxyacetanilide P-acetamido phenol commonly known as paracetamol</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="trade-name">Trade Name<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trade-name" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Trademarks, trade names, brand names and proprietary names are interchangeable terms used to identify drugs manufactured by various drug companies. A specific generic drug may have various trade names.</p>
<p>The symbol after the trade name indicates that the trade name is registered and its use is restricted to the manufacturer who owns it. Trade names may be selected to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Denote the drug's chemical structure</li>
<li>Identify the company responsible for manufacturing the drug</li>
<li>Represent some property of the drug</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples of trade names include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chlordiazepoxide, referred to as Librium</li>
<li>Chlorpromazine, referred to as Largactil</li>
<li>Paracetamol, referred to as Calpol, Cetal, PMC, Panadol, Panleve, Panok, Labalgin and so on</li>
</ul>
<p>No other firms or company can employ the same trade name. A trade name is usually selected to be short, catchy and easy to pronounce.</p>
<p>Examples of Names Given to Some Common Drugs</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Generic Name</th><th>Chemical Name</th><th>Trade Name(s)</th><th>Commonly Used Abbreviation</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Asprin</td><td>Acetylsalicylic acid</td><td>Ecotin</td><td>ASA</td></tr><tr><td>Milk of Magnesium</td><td>Magnesium hydroxide</td><td>Phillips milk of Magnesia</td><td>MOM</td></tr><tr><td>Tetracycline</td><td>Hydrochloride of 4-(dimethylamino)-1,4a,5,5a,6,11,12a-octahydro-3,6,10,12,12a-pentahydroxy-6-mythyl-1,11-dioxa-2-napthacene carboxamide.</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Prednisone</td><td>11B,17,21-trihydroxypregna-1, 4-diene-3-20-dione</td><td>Deltasone Meticorten Cortigel Cortophi ngel</td><td>ACTH</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-family">Drug Family<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-family" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Drugs may be classified in many ways. One substance may belong to more than one family depending on the classification used. A drug may be designated by its chemical derivation, for example, heavy metals, xanthines, steroids, phenothiazines and so on.</p>
<p>Drugs may also be grouped according to the mechanism of action, for example, central nervous system depressant, anti-cholinergic, anti-inflammatory and others. In other words, drugs with similar characteristics are often grouped together in families.</p>
<p>The family name may denote its:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chemical structure, for example, barbiturate</li>
<li>Mode of action, for example, antacid</li>
<li>Physiologic action, for example, diuretic</li>
<li>Therapeutic effect, for example, anticonvulsant, analgesic</li>
</ul>
<p>A drug may also be listed under more than one classification, for instance, aspirin, which is an analgesic, antipyretic, and anti-inflammatory drug.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
